# Side Story 25 – Orihime (Rir) and Hikoboshi (Shuu)

In times long past, on the side of the milky way, there lived a good (played by Shuu’s father this time).

Said god had a son, Shuu, who was also nicknamed Hikoboshi. He was academically and athletically gifted, and some said that he even surpassed human limits. His handsome features naturally caused beautiful girls to gather around him. To onlookers, he seemed popular and possessed of perfect qualities.

He had four childhood friends that could be described as peerless beauties, but sadly they were already in love with each other, so he couldn’t lay hands on them. Furthermore, two of them were male. Heedless of that fact, Shuu kept an amicable relationship with them as he steeled his muscles, trained his skills, and studied hard in order to join the carrier group of the cosmic guardians.

The god, unable to overlook this any further, spoke with his son.

“Shuu. You are already of age, so won’t you find a woman or two?”  

“Well, I’m good right now. Maybe after I found a job…”  

“That’s an option, but your mother and I were your age when we met. I never had another romantic encounter after joining the cosmic guardians, you see?”  

“I understand, Father. In that case, what should I do…?”  

“Well, that doesn’t mean you have to rush things. You have time to find someone from now until you graduate from university.”  

“Right.”

It was a holiday, and the father and son were walking through the city.

“Woof… matches… won’t anyone buy my matches?”

A girl about the same age as Shuu, who was wearing a suffocating-looking outfit consisting of a red hood, long sleeved jacket, and long pants, even though it was the middle of summer, was walking around, trying to sell the matches her basket was stuffed full of. However, from how many there were left, she apparently hadn’t sold any.

“She’s wearin’ all that in this insane heat… and she’s sellin’ matches?”  

“She must be extremely sensitive to the cold. And it doesn’t look like anyone’s buying.”  

“Looks like it… Still, I feel like I know her from somewhere…”

It happened while the two were talking.

“Matches… ah… woof…”

The young girl collapsed into a heap.

“Look, that’s what happens if you dress up like that!”  

“There’s probably another reason.”

The two of them rushed to the girl.

“She’s not sweating, her pulse is racing, and her skin has turned pink. It’s a severe case of heatstroke… Shuu.”  

“Right.”

While the god contacted a hospital, Shuu picked up the girl and carried her to some nearby shade. In the process, the hood fell from her head.

“…What the hell?”  

“Yes, I’m calling because of a girl with heatstroke… Is something wrong, Shuu?”  

“This girl… she has horrible scars…”  

“What!?”

_____  

___  

_

Things moved quickly afterwards.

At the hospital, it turned out the girl was covered in numerous hideous both new and old wounds, and the god who held a high position in the cosmic guardians determined that she had been ordered under the threat of punishment to go around selling matches in the middle of summer. Ultimately, the married couple who had taken her in were arrested for various crimes.

“…What’s your name?”  

“I am called… Rir, though some also call me Orihime. Uhm… thank you… for saving me.”  

“Nah, doin’ that was natural.”

The girl Rir, who had only woken up three days after she collapsed with heatstroke, was talking with Shuu for the first time. Before that, the god had come to her and explained what happened.

“…U-Uhm.”  

“What’s up?”  

“I-It feels… like you saved me once before. Last year…”  

“Oh, I know! You’re that girl who was about to fall from the bridge, right?”  

“Yes, that was me! Thank you so much for rescuing me several times.”  

“Don’t mention it.”

As they were talking, the god entered the room.

“…Miss Rir.”  

“Ah… you’re the one who freed me from those people… I am grateful to you, but… what am I supposed to do now…?”  

“Why not join our family?”  

“Woof!?”  

“Father!?”

Both the son and the girl seemed stunned at the sudden suggestion.

“Our family only has one child. Why not add another? Besides…”

The god looked at both Shuu and Rir. He could already see some connection between them.

“The two of you know each other, don’t you?”  

“I-I guess?”  

“I-I suppose that’s true.”  

“Moreover…”

The god got closer to Rir and whispered something to her. She seemed flabbergasted.

“Y-You think so…!? But I’m covered in scars!”  

“He’s not someone who is bothered by such a thing. Right, Shuu? You think she’s cute, even with all those scars, don’t you?  

“Sure, she’s super cute… Hang on, what the hell are you makin’ me say, Dad!?”  

“Woof!?”

The two of them, just as the god predicted, later started a relationship and got married a few years down the line. Their anniversary was the seventh of July; a date that would become a holiday.

---

**TL notes:**  

We end volume 19 with another weird side story that begins like side story 6 but then veers off to a version of the little match girl but in the middle of summer instead of the dead of winter and with heatstroke instead of freezing to death. At least the girl survives here.

Anyway, volume 19 was, as feared at the start, not super riveting, but at least an improvement over volume 18 in my opinion. It remains to be seen how the guide arc will develop, through with the author, once more, giving away a surprise in advance, I’m somewhat doubtful. Only time will tell.

**There will be a week-long pause between volume 19 and 20, mainly for me to finally go over older chapters and fix the formatting issues.**

# 597 – A Day Without Kanata – 1 (Sakura)

Sakura was in her Room with too much time on her hands and nothing to do.

Due to fall’s middle school athletics competition drawing near, plus her being a member of the “going home club”, classes had ended early for her. On that note, there was a similar event for high school students.

Normally, she’d be playing games with Kanata or walk around town with him, but the boy in question wasn’t present since he “made a promise to come to the research institute right after school ended.” Furthermore, her older sister and her future brother-in-law – the others with whom she’d normally spend time – had gone off somewhere to flirt and make out. It wasn’t her place to get in their way.

“…I’m bored.”

Back when she had been practically blind, she used to go to bed early, but now that felt like a huge waste, so she instead pulled out her smartphone. But she immediately recalled that she didn’t have anything of interest on it, so she put it away again and flopped down on her bed.

“I guess I could go to Kanata’s room…”

With that sudden thought, she opened her own window right away and the one opposite leading to her boyfriend’s room, which she knew usually wasn’t locked.

“…Hang on, what am I doing? Even if he’s my boyfriend, doing that when he’s not there is just rude.”

At that realization, she was about to head back to her room, when something caught her attention.

She looked around the room. At a glance, it seemed rather plain. The only decorations were a few photographs of the boy and her, and some of him with his family. Well, that obviously wasn’t everything, but apart from the usual things you’d expect to find in the room of someone with a case of eight grader’s syndrome – like an intricately drawn magic circle of unknown origin – the place was quite modest.

“I thought he stopped acting so much like a chuunibyou lately, but I guess he’s still the same. Thinking back, he started obsessing about eye patches and bandages pretty much from the moment he had a grasp of the world around himself. He’ll probably stay that way even as an adult.”

Sakura thought back fondly on the past, which caused her to recall an event.

“Kanata…”

It was from her early childhood. When the research institute had cast its eye on the boy.

“…I guess all I did was cause him trouble.”

The boy was a child prodigy. At one year of age, he had learned enough words to hold normal conversations, and at two, he was already able to read the newspaper and simple novels. At three, he had amassed a wealth of knowledge unthinkable of an infant. He was even able to speak English.

But from that point, he stopped acting in a way that made him stand out “in public”. He entered the same normal preschool as Sakura, followed by the same grade school, before finally taking the entry exam and enrolling with her at the middle school part of a combined school and university that was said to be one of the best in Japan. At that time, Sakura had to frantically study for the entry exam of said school.

Back then, Sakura, who was practically blind unless she wore special glasses and considered herself inferior to her peers in all aspects save her intellect, used to think that the boy was merely humoring her. With his talents and knowledge, he could’ve attended a university in Europe or the US when he was eight years old.

But he ended up neglecting his studies. He even started half-assing their exams at school (though he still did enough to get a passing mark). That was what he limited himself to in public.

Still, Sakura had vague knowledge about him already developing new technologies behind the scenes at the research institute and making some marvelous achievements.

“…Just why did he put up with me? Was it to watch over me, after all? Or… or maybe because he loved me all that time? Eh-heh-heh.”

Sakura felt bashfully happy at that thought. Though from an outside perspective, it likely looked rather suspicious. She suddenly glanced at Kanata’s bed. Both the pillow and futon were clean and neatly folded.

“I’m… I’m sure he won’t mind… if it’s just a bit, right? We’re dating, so he probably won’t complain… right?”

She dove onto her boyfriend’s bed. Then, she buried her face in his pillow.

“Kanata… I love you! I love you so much…!” she exclaimed, muffling her voice enough so she wouldn’t be overheard.

After getting her fill of the boy’s warmth, she got off the bed and, after putting it back in order, started thinking again.

“Acting like this makes me no better than Sis back then… He won’t find out and hate me for it, will he?”

She suddenly got a bad feeling. At that moment, the door to the room opened.

“Cleaning, cleaning… time for- Oh, Sakura!”  

“A-Aunty!”

It was Ayumu’s and Kanata’s mother, who’d usually be at work at that time. By coincidence, she had finished early at her job and was now about to clean the house.

Sakura was in an awful fluster… but at the same time, she was relieved that it hadn’t happened when she was lying on the boy’s bed.

“Have you come to play, Sakura?”  

“Eh, uhm, y-yes. Erm… Kanata isn’t home and Big Sis and Ayu-nii are doing something by the two of them… so I didn’t have anything to do… I’m sorry.”  

“It’s alright, we already see you like our own daughter. Don’t you agree?”  

“E-Eh-heh-heh, I guess so.”

Sakura felt awkward at her actions getting official approval.

Her future mother-in-law put down the cleaning implements and spoke up again.

“Why don’t you come relax downstairs? Or did you just come to find things about Kanata to nitpick?”  

“Ah… u-uhm.”

The older woman gave a slightly suspicious grin as she watched the flustered girl.

“If you don’t have anything to do, there’s a video I’ve been wanting to show you. About Kanata. I thought about showing you since the two of you started dating, but there was never a good opportunity.”

Sakura’s eyes went wide when she heard about such a video’s existence. Before she knew it, she found herself nodding.

“Alright, then it’s settled. Come on down.”  

“Y-Yes!”

The two of them went to the living room.

---

**TL notes:**  

We start volume 20 with a three-parter of Sakura reminiscing and learning more about Kanata.

A short time ago, I complained about a character in a different story acting almost insultingly stupidly. A reply I got was that it’s genuinely hard to write a truly brilliant character and it’s much easier to make other characters stupid to make someone seem brilliant.

Here, we hear a lot about Kanata’s supposed brilliance, but while he seemed somewhat insightful in the Yggdrasil arc, it was hardly the kind of genius he’s apparently meant to exhibit. A true genius might have found flaws in Anazumu’s system to exploit and/or solved the whole Surtr situation in a completely different way that no one could’ve predicted. Maybe that’s just me expecting too much, but it certainly feels like another instance of “tell don’t show”.

Anyway, with 41 chapters, volume 20 will be shorter than volume 19 (though that’s mainly due to the absence of side stories) and seems to focus on the identity of the Guide and Shuu’s Judo competition.

+++

# 598 – A Day Without Kanata – 2 (Sakura)

“Where was it… ah, here!”

The woman brought out a storage medium. It had been recently developed and was high-performance for video files, superior to traditional products[1](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-598-a-day-without-kanata-2-sakura/#easy-footnote-bottom-1-119259).

“What is the video about?”  

“Let me think, it’s from eight years ago, so… Kanata was around six at the time.”  

“Huh…”  

“It’s from that research institute. As a matter of fact, they regularly send us the recordings of some of their experiments.”

This was something Sakura heard for the first time. Heedless of the girl’s surprise, the woman plugged the storage device into the TV with practiced motions and opened the video file selection.

“That’s the one I wanted to show you, Sakura. Well, there are many other things I’d like to ask you about, but for now have a seat.”  

“O-Of course.”

She did as she had been told and sat down on the sofa. Kanata’s mother used the remote control to select one of the videos and started the playback. This experimental record apparently consisted of an interview about everyday things.

On the other side of the screen was a young Kanata, indistinguishable from a pretty girl, which made nostalgic feelings rush through Sakura. All the same, this was the first time she got a proper look at how the young Kanata had looked like, and she was shocked at how feminine he appeared.

“Kanata, he was incredibly cute…”  

“He resembles his other brother in that… Well, even my husband and I were undoubtedly so as kids.”

On the screen, Kanata seemed to be waiting for something as he sat on his own on a stool. When about a minute had passed, a researcher arrived, who didn’t show up on screen but instead sat down somewhere next to the camera.

_“I kept you waiting.”_  

_“I don’t mind.”_ the six-year-old Kanata replied in a surprisingly composed tone.

His big, round eyes seemed to move between the researcher and the camera.

_“In that case, can we start with the usual questions? How old are you currently?”  

“I’m six.”  

“You just started grade school, haven’t you?”  

“Yes, I have.”_

He seemed quite happy in his reply. Anyone seeing this would assume the boy had fun at school.

_“Do you enjoy school?”  

“I do! I get to meet lots of different people!”  

“I see, that’s good to hear… Do you like it more than preschool?”  

“…It’s too early to tell. I should at least experience it for one month.”  

“You have a point there.”_

The researcher seemed to be writing something down.

_“With your IQ… no, your talents, you could surely pass the entry exam for a university if you studied for it. Many past geniuses at your level did so… why not you? Could you tell me your reason?”  

“That’s easy to answer. It would be a huge waste, wouldn’t it?”  

“A waste, you say…?”_

The young Kanata nodded while smiling. The researcher made another note.

_“Why is that?”  

“I want friends my own age, and I read in a book that you go on a school trip in the sixth year of grade school! Going to university without experiencing the things you can only do when you’re young would be a waste[2](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-598-a-day-without-kanata-2-sakura/#easy-footnote-bottom-2-119259)!”  

“Oh-ho… I see, so that’s your train of thought.”_

For some reason, the researcher seemed happy. Maybe it was because the answer was unexpected or maybe because it contradicted past data.

_“But all the other students around you will be clearly less capable. Ever the teachers might be inferior to you. I can only imagine class being boring for you. How do you think about that?”  

“It’s true, that part scares me, so I’m only half paying attention to class and spend the rest of the time sleeping or doing other things!”  

“Ha, ha-ha-ha. You mean to say you’re slacking off?”  

“…I am.”_

The researcher laughed at the boy’s brazen declaration. Kanata’s mother and Sakura also broke into smiles.

“He’s making good on that promise…”  

“Isn’t he…? I honestly didn’t think he’d keep it up. That’s why your exam scores surpassed his, Sakura.”  

“That’s true!”

On the screen, the researcher and Kanata were still talking.

_“Next, I want to ask you something about your childhood friend, Sakura.”_

“Huh!?”

Sakura’s eyes went wide when she heard her own name, and she listened even more closely.

_“Ok.”  

“We do know quite a lot about her. You also told us of her several times. At the age of three, she became unable to see without the aid of glasses due to an accident, correct?”  

“Yes, that’s correct.”_

The boy’s childish and lovely face turned serious. Anyone would’ve been astonished at a six-year-old giving such a knowing look.

_“Who is she to you? Couldn’t having a blind friend turn out disadvantageous for you?”  

“From my perspective, Sakura is…”_

From the change in the boy’s voice, it could be heard that he was reluctant to answer the question[3](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-598-a-day-without-kanata-2-sakura/#easy-footnote-bottom-3-119259). Still with a grim look, he was about to give his reply. Sakura pricked her ears.

_“…She is someone I have to protect.”  

“Someone you have to protect? Why?”  

“When she lost the ability to see, it was as if something inside me also disappeared.”_

The researcher jotted down another note. The earlier relaxed atmosphere was nowhere to be found, instead having turned into a mirror of the boy’s frigid expression.

_“I still don’t know what that was. But I have to protect her… I’m not sure how to put it.”  

“Is it your sense of duty?”  

“That’s it. A sense of duty.”_

At this point, Sakura was completely engrossed in the boy’s words. The Kanata’s mother gave a chuckle as she looked at the girl.

#### Footnotes:

1. I’m not sure where the author is going with this. This was written in 2017, so 4K-HD blue rays weren’t anything new, plus you’d rather use a USB storage for a video like the one described here. Sure, those regularly get bigger capacities and writing/reading speed improves, but that’s more of a gradual process.[](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-598-a-day-without-kanata-2-sakura/#easy-footnote-1-119259)

2. I guess if you have to choose between soul-crushingly hard studies while being unable to connect with your peers, and being bored while having the possibility to take things slow, find friends, and enjoy yourself, the latter does seem more attractive.[](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-598-a-day-without-kanata-2-sakura/#easy-footnote-2-119259)

3. The original makes it sound like it’s the researcher reluctant to reply, which wouldn’t make sense, so I assume that’s an error.[](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-598-a-day-without-kanata-2-sakura/#easy-footnote-3-119259)

# 599 – A Day Without Kanata – 3 (Sakura)

_“In that case, let’s change the question. I’ll go straight to the point, do you like Sakura?”_  

_“Yes, I like her a lot!”_ Kanata replied with a carefree smile, a complete change from how he’d just been.

Sakura involuntarily blushed.

_“Do you want to marry her in the future?”  

“…Oh, in that kind of meaning? C-Can I speak freely?”  

“No one else can see this, just voice your thoughts[1](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-599-a-day-without-kanata-3-sakura/#easy-footnote-bottom-1-119261).”  

“…Really? In the future… if Sakura feels the same way and… uhm, if no one gets between us and we properly start dating… I guess.”_

Sakura made sure to commit the contrast of the boy speaking so seriously while nervously fidgeting to memory. At the same time, it filled her with happiness to learn that he held those feelings for her, even when he’d been so young.

_“This might be a rude question, but won’t your daily life be incredibly difficult with her and-“_  

_“Didn’t I say earlier that I’ll protect her?”_ Kanata interrupted the researcher, giving a stare that was closer to a glare. _“I resolved myself to do that ever since I can remember.”_

While the question had been led with an apology, it was clear that it enraged the boy.

_“S-Sorry… So, you like her that much.”  

“I do… But she doesn’t know. I don’t think she sees me like that.”_

“(Now that he mentions it… how did I feel back then?)”

Sakura thought back to the past and recalled things bit by bit. The recording was paused.

“How did you feel back then, Sakura? About Kanata, I mean.”  

“…I think it’s like he said it. I probably had feelings for him since I remember.”  

“Friendly ones… or those of love?”  

“Th-Th-The latter…”

Mrs. Joujou looked at the blushing girl with a grin and then resumed the video playback.

_“Hm~, I wonder about that. If you ask me… no, I shouldn’t bring my own feelings into this. By the way, what is your dream for the future, Kanata?”  

“To find a way to restore eyesight. Be that via drugs, on the cellular level, or with technology. So Sakura can see again.”  

“Right, you mentioned that before.”_

Sakura had also known about that dream. This was another thing he did for her sake.

_“That will be the final question, then… If Sakura were to find someone else she likes in the future and were to marry them, how would you feel about that?”  

“…Give me a moment.”_

Kanata’s expression turned serious again. Sakura swallowed as she gazed at the screen. Kanata’s mother was grinning.

_“I would be fine with it, if they make her happy. But if they made her cry, I’d never forgive them. For me, Sakura is like a-”  

“Like what?”  

“Like a princess… I guess?”_

Sakura caught a glimpse of the true feelings of the little boy on the screen, who looked so much like an innocently smiling girl. It brought her profound happiness.

_“Does that mean you’re her knight?”  

“A knight! Heh-heh, I like that, it makes me feel all excited!”  

“E-Excited?”_

At this point, the recording ended. Kanata’s mother pulled the storage device from the TV with a somewhat warm expression.

“So, are you going to let him protect you from now on, too?”

Sakura nodded with a smile. She couldn’t help but feel that she finally understood how her childhood friend, who always seemed too smart for her to grasp, really thought.

“In the end, I can’t imagine being with anyone but him, either…”  

“I see! I guess that means the day we get to see our grandchildren won’t be far.”  

“G-G-G-Grandchildren!? W-We’re still too young to have children… A-Anyway, won’t Big Sis and Ayu-nii be before us?”  

“That’s true…”

As Sakura blushed for what felt like the fifth time, there was a shadow on the porch. Moments after Kanata’s mother noticed it, the door opened.

“I’m back.”  

“Welcome home, Kanata!”  

“K-Kanata!!”  

“Huh? You’re here, Sakura?”

The girl rushed over to him. The moment he had entered her field of vision, she’d gone for a hug.

“Kanata… I love you…!”  

“Uhm, yes. I love you, too… Mom, what happened to Sakura?”  

“She seemed bored, so I called her over and told her stories about how devoted you are to her.”  

“Eh…”

Even though her future mother-in-law was watching, Sakura, in a rare case, didn’t show any embarrassment as she let the boy keep spoiling her. Kanata seemed to be at a loss, as he was stroking her head.

“For now, let’s go upstairs,” she proposed.  

“My, I’m sure your older sister told you that too,” the older woman interjected, “but at least wait until you’re in high school before you do that kind of stuff.”  

“I… I know that!”

Still in a tight embrace, Kanata dexterously slipped of his shoes and entered the house. It was a skill he’d acquired over the past decade he spent with the then blind Sakura.

“Kanata~…”  

“I wonder what your mother would say if she saw you so clingy, Sakura…” Mrs. Joujou teased.  

“Heh-heh!”

Before long, the two of them were in Kanata’s room. Sakura immediately hugged the boy again.

“Can I… kiss you?”  

“S-Sure.”

Kanata suffered an instant knock out, as his childhood friend asked him that with upturned eyes while in his embrace. He almost automatically accepted her request. As usual, they simply pressed their lips together, but that was enough for them.

“Eh-heh-heh-heh.”  

“I guess I can indulge you every now and then. Though it also helps that you’re so cute. Ah, before I forget, there was another matter.”  

“Hm? What is it?”

Kanata turned serious like he had done in the recording.

“Lately, it feels like there’s someone following us, so you should be careful.”  

“Really…? Alright.”  

“Yeah, I noticed it since the start of this week…”

He felt certain that someone really followed them, and that it wasn’t caused by something he’d seen on TV. He moved his eyes to Sakura, who was still clinging to him.

“This time, can I kiss you?”  

“Bwuh… Kanata…? Sure, that’s fine with me!”

#### Footnotes:

1. And then they send it to the parents. I can’t imagine much trust was left after this.[](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-599-a-day-without-kanata-3-sakura/#easy-footnote-1-119261)

# 600 – Someone is Stalking Us?

“Why did we meet here?”

It was Friday. For some reason, I was suddenly called here for lunch. This was a combined school, so if we wanted, we could eat lunch in the middle school portion, but why did both Kanata and Shuu call me here?

“Lately, some creep keeps followin’ us.”  

“Yes. Though it hasn’t caused any issues, yet.”  

“What!?”

_That’s bad! Sakura, and Rir are cute enough, it wouldn’t be unnatural for someone to stalk them… It happened to Mika and me in the past. Well, we somehow managed with the help of Shuu and his father._

_Oh, if you’re wondering, the people stalking me were obviously men._

“Don’t tell me there’s a stalker greedy enough to go after both Rir and Sakura at the same time…!?”  

“Doesn’t feel that way…”  

“But we can’t exclude the possibility.”

_Scary. When men get like that (stalkers, molesters, and such…) things turn truly frightening. If what they say is true, then this is a grave matter._

“Moreover, what if they target you and Mika-nee too, Bro? I mean, you’re the one who lets his mind wander[1](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-600-someone-is-stalking-us/#easy-footnote-bottom-1-119263) the most among us. It just feels off that you’re the only one who didn’t notice anything.”  

“Hey, that’s mean! Hmph!”  

“That don’t change the fact you gotta watch out. I also told Pops, just in case.”

If Shuu’s father was keeping an eye out, then there was no safer place on Earth. He was a policeman, after all. But Kanata still looked as gloomy as before.

“If it’s a normal person, then relying on Shuu’s father should be enough. Even supposing it isn’t, I could ask the research institute to lend us some bodyguards, which would likely solve the issue…”  

“True… But you’re worried ’bout somethin’ else, ain’t you, Kanata. Same goes for me.”  

“Yes. If this is connected to Anazumu, then it won’t be that easy.”

_Huh, looks like it’s just the two of them discussing things now. I feel a bit left out… Hang on? To begin with, why do they give off this vibe of working together on this case?_

“Come to think of it, when have the two of you discussed this?”  

“Well, Kanata contacted me, sayin’ it felt like someone was stalkin’ him and wantin’ do consult with me before it got bad.”  

“And when I did… I learned that it was the same for Shuu. We both thought that it felt suspicious. That was yesterday.”

_I see, they both felt something was off, so they got in contact, and now they called me here to warn me. I’m grateful for that. I am, but…_

“Kanata, why didn’t you come to me, your older brother, first? You should rely on me more! Hmph!”  

“Well, that’s because you look like a girl, Bro. A. Girl. You’d just become another victim…”  

“Then why didn’t you tell Mom and Dad?”  

“I’m pretty sure Shuu and his father are more reliable than our parents when it comes to stalkers.”

If he put it like that, I had no room to argue. Our countermeasures when dealing with stalkers had always been to rely on the Hinos.

“Bah. In any case, we need to watch out.”  

“I’ll protect Sakura in case anything happens, so we’ll be fine.”  

“Same for Rir and me.”

_People are stronger when they have someone to protect… usually._  

_As for Kanata and me… he’s got his smart, but I’m not sure what I have going for me. I’m not strong, at least on this side._

“How are we going to deal with it? You’ll be at the intra scholastic tournament on the weekend, Shuu, and you’ll be on a date with Sakura in the Zoo this Sunday, right, Kanata? I also promised Mika[2](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-600-someone-is-stalking-us/#easy-footnote-bottom-2-119263) to go grape picking with her.”

_Won’t it be dangerous if someone assaults us while we we’re so spread out? But they can’t just call off the tournament and date._

“I’m sure we’ll manage somehow.”  

“We all have a packed schedule… At any rate, grape picking sounds like a nice idea. I might give that a try with Sakura, too.”

_So, the two of them think they’ll be fine for now? Well, if my brother says so, he must be certain. Hm~, we should still come up with some countermeasures._

“When we’re back in Anazumu, let’s all train in self-defense techniques.”  

“True, that should work.”

With Secret Martial Techniques, we should be able to move on the level of the best professional martial artists[3](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-600-someone-is-stalking-us/#easy-footnote-bottom-3-119263) (or even better).

“That was all we wanted to tell you,” Kanata declared, as if to bring our talk to a close.

Shuu nodded in agreement.

“There’s only 15 minutes left of our lunch break, so let’s disperse… Oh, by the way, Shuu, when should we come to the tournament to cheer you on?”  

“Ah, thanks ’bout that.” Shuu looked happy as he scratched his head.

I always came to cheer him on at some point. I mean, we were best friends.

“Durin’ the regional tournament you’ll be on your dates, and we’ll win that one anyway, so no need to root for us. You can wait with that until we get to the prefectural part.”  

“What do you mean, you’ll win anyway… is that a given? Still, thanks.”

After talking for a bit longer, we split up.

_A stalker, huh…? I need to watch out. Those guys are scary._

#### Footnotes:

1. The original is 気が抜ける (“to lose interest”, “to lose flavor”) and context makes it sound like it was meant to be 気を抜く (“to lose focus”, “to let one’s mind wander”), though the first might also work.[](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-600-someone-is-stalking-us/#easy-footnote-1-119263)

2. Sakura in the original. An obvious error.[](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-600-someone-is-stalking-us/#easy-footnote-2-119263)

3. Only if they also train with the skills on Earth. Otherwise, the stat difference would surely throw them off too much.

# 601 – The Judo Tournament (Shuu)

“Alright, first is the team competition!”

It was finally time for the intra scholastic tournament’s regional team competition! Incidentally, the individual competition would be tomorrow.

By the team competition’s rules, we fought in teams of five. The order the team members fought was vanguard, second, center, vice-captain, and finally captain[1](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-601-the-judo-tournament-shuu/#easy-footnote-bottom-1-119265). If you lost, you dropped out, and if you won, you stayed in the game and fought the opposing team’s next in line. Ultimately, the team with the least combined individual defeats won.

It was possible for the captain to turn everything around and defeat the whole opposing team on their own, so you couldn’t let your guard down.

“Anyway, it’s our job to reduce the burden on the club head!”  

“And if possible, win this thing without him ever being needed!”

There was laughter. It looked like none of them were nervous. The previous seniors in the team had all graduated, so it now consisted of four second-years and one very talented fist-year.

As a result of training solely with me without interruption, Gouda had improved so much in the span of a single day, he apparently couldn’t believe it himself. Gorilla Sensei had asked me to do that, and afterwards I repeated the same with the other members who’d compete in the team fights. I could’ve done this for the better part of a year, so I felt a bit bad for starting so late.

“Let’s go!”  

“””YEAAAAAAAAH!!”””

We formed the usual group circle. Rir, the group’s only woman, was between our instructor and me. She’d said she’d do her best to cheer us on.

The circle was dissolved, and everyone found a place in the waiting room.

Incidentally, I was the team captain and Gouda the vice-captain. The sole first-year formed the vanguard, and the second and center were filled by the remaining two second-years who were balanced in their abilities, so they usually took their team position by preference.

The first-year vanguard, Hoshino[2](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-601-the-judo-tournament-shuu/#easy-footnote-bottom-2-119265), was shouting things like “I’ll beat the whole team myself! I’ll steal the spotlight from you, Seniors! Ha-ha-ha!” so I had high expectations for him. When I trained with him the day before yesterday, he’d genuinely improved by a lot.

“Shuu, you can do it! It’s only the regional competition, so it’s probably easy, but don’t let it get to your head!”  

“Right. Thanks, Rir.”

Yesterday after training was over, she had given me a massage. Not sure where she picked up the skill, probably somewhere in Anazumu, but before I knew it, she had turned into a massage-pro. With her slender hands, she did her utmost to help unknot my muscles. It was cute, awfully cute.

Along the way, maybe because she started massaging parts that weren’t exactly needed, or because she gave permission for me to touch her too, it turned into a very different kind of massage, though that was likely something that happened only between lovers.

_I do have a wonderful girlfriend. Lucky me._

“…Do you want a kiss?”  

“…We ain’t at home, so not on the mouth.”  

“Woof, alright!” she replied before pulling me into an embrace and pressing a kiss on my cheek.

_Suddenly, I’m super hyped up! Well, it’s possible I don’t get a turn today. Even without me, our team is said to be the strongest._

“God damn it, I’m so jealous! I’m way too jealous of you!”  

“You got all intimate yesterday, didn’t you? It shows.”

These comments came from Futayama and Nakagawa[3](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-601-the-judo-tournament-shuu/#easy-footnote-bottom-3-119265), the second and center of the team. These guys always made jealous jabs when Rir and I were talking.

“…W-Well, she’s my girlfriend, ain’t she?”  

“Ugh…”  

“Grrrrrrrrr.”

At this point, they looked like they might start crying blood any moment. Thinking of it, the two of them were friends and neither of the two had ever dated someone.

_I mean, I was the same until I met Rir, but those two are pretty popular with girls at this point, so how dare they complain? I just don’t get them._

“In any case, please do you best, Futayama!”  

“I-I will…!”

Rir had grasped Futayama’s hand with both of hers. The boy in question turned red and fell silent.

“The same goes for you Nakagawa, alright?”  

“Y-Yes’m!”

She did the same with Nakagawa. When did she learn to captivate men just by grasping their hands?

“Hoshino, do your best, too, alright? We expect much from you!”  

“Y-Yesh! I’ll do my besht!”

In the same vein, she walked up to our vanguard and took his hand. Still, he seemed way too hyped up.  

_Well, that’s ’cause Rir’s so cute._

“Gouda, please do your best to support Shuu.”  

“You can count on me.”

Gouda was last. It didn’t show on his face, but I was sure that he inwardly reacted the same as Nakagawa and the others.

Afterwards, she proclaimed that she’d be rooting us, which was followed by excited shouts. She then returned to my side.

“Rir, when did you learn to deal with people like Ayumu?”  

“Woof? I only told them to do their best and that I’d be cheering them on? What does that have to do with Alim?”  

“Well, don’t worry ’bout it.”

Guess that just now was her own talent. She might have the natural makings of an idol… Heh, but she’s my dear girlfriend. It probably won’t turn into some huge deal like with Ayumu.

“I told you earlier, but do your best! I’ve seen you work hard for months now, so I know you can do it!”  

“Right, with you rootin’ for me, I have superhuman strength.”

I impulsively patted her head.

_Now, time to get serious! Just like last year, let’s aim for the national tournament and win this!_

#### Footnotes:

1. My quick Google search didn’t yield any official English names for these team positions, so these names might be off.[](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-601-the-judo-tournament-shuu/#easy-footnote-1-119265)

2. Been a while since we had new names. This one has multiple possible readings with the original being 星野 (lit. Star Plain).[](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-601-the-judo-tournament-shuu/#easy-footnote-2-119265)

3. Two more names with multiple possible readings. The originals are 二山 (lit. Two Mountains) and 中川 (lit. Middle of the River).[](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-601-the-judo-tournament-shuu/#easy-footnote-3-119265)

# 602 – Grape Picking

It was Sunday.

Mika and I were appropriately dressed for going to the forest and had already placed a reservation at the place where we were planning to harvest grapes (the all-you-can-eat variant).

On another note, Shuu’s team got first place at the regional competition. Well, that wasn’t surprising. With him in the team, they were sure to make it to the national tournament.

But from what I heard, he had no chance at all to shine in the regional tournament. Apparently, the only first-year in their team who’d been entrusted with the role of vanguard had performed so well, he practically won the whole thing by himself. He only lost one or two fights, leaving those to the club member who fulfilled the role of second, but those two pretty much dominated the whole tournament. It was incredible.

The prefectural tournament would probably go the same way. I’d still come to watch as I’d promised. If I had the time, I’d also have come to the regional tournament.

“Hey, we definitely should take some grapes with us home, right?” Mika wondered.  

“We should! Let’s bring everyone souvenirs.”  

“That would be Sakura and Kanata, my parents and yours… then Shuu and Rir, and Shuu’s parents…”  

“Q-Quite a few people.”

By that calculation, we’ll have to bring at least ten bushels back with us. Hm~, taking six bushels each on our way home will just barely work out.

“Sakura loves sweets, so we should bring another bushel for her, and then another for Shuu in celebration of their victory, which would make a total of 12. I suppose we do have our satchels, but it might be best to split them up to take six bushels each.”  

“L-Let’s do that.”

I was left with no choice but to go along with Mika’s suggestion; we would split up our harvest as we brought it home. Grapes weren’t that heavy, but the bushels took a lot of space.

“We’re here.”  

“We are.”

A short time later, we arrived at the place where we’d put in the reservation. For 1600 Yen, you could harvest as much as you wanted within two hours. They had a total of five different types, including Kyoho, Delaware, and Muscat grapes.  

_How in the world is that profitable for the farmer? I don’t get it._

I’d been here once with my family in the past, and the quality of the grapes wasn’t bad at all. Well, since it apparently worked out, Mika and I would simply enjoy ourselves.

“Alright, let’s go gather!”  

“Let’s go, let’s go!”

We borrowed small baskets and then made our way to an area where many grapevines could be found. It looked like this place had Delaware grapes.

“Those look tasty! Ugh, can’t reach them…”

Even though a fair number of grapes grew at a height that Mika could easily reach with her around 160 centimeters, she deliberately stood on her tiptoes, trying to get some that grew higher up. She then shot me a glance.

_I suppose I’ll meet her expectations._

“Here you go, Your Highness.”  

“Thank you, My Lady!”  

“…Ugh.”  

“Eh-heh-heh, I’m joking. Thanks, you were very handsome.”

She smiled as she signaled with her hand that I’d done a good job.  

_Gah, way too cute. That’s how a date should feel._

We each put a bushel of Delaware grapes into our baskets and found a nearby place to sit, where we started to eat them.

“Mmh! So sweet!”  

“You’re right… delicious…”  

“Here you go, say ‘ah’.”  

“Ah.”

She fed me some of her grapes. Thus, I did the same.

“Here, Mika, say ‘ah’.”  

“Ah~.”

Most likely on purpose, she licked my fingers slightly as she ate the grapes from my hand. Today, she seemed a bit aggressive.

“Heh-heh, so sweet.”  

“Should we set our sights on the huge, round ones, next?”  

“Huge, round ones… hang on, don’t you dare look at me like that! My chest might be big, but… Oh, you were talking about Kyoho grapes[1](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-602-grape-picking/#easy-footnote-bottom-1-119267). Sorry.”

I stared at Mika who’d suddenly started to spout this nonsense. Either way, we decided to look for Kyoho grapes next.

“This area is rather crowded, isn’t it?”  

“You’re right.”

Now that she mentioned it, there were lots of families visiting this place. It was also Sunday. Including us, there were around 10 groups. But I couldn’t make out any people by themselves or groups solely consisting of men or women, so we could probably relax regarding that stalker affair.

While pondering these thoughts, we gathered Kyoho grapes before finding another nearby place to sit and eat a bushel each.

“Oh, so yummy. They’re sweet and super tasty.”  

“We should take that sort back with us.”  

“Yeah. Let’s add Muscat grapes for Sakura and Shuu.”

Afterwards, we first ate a bushel of the other three sorts and then made a quick round to get those we liked most. Gathering grapes by the two of us while flirting and making out took longer than expected. There was also the time we spent eating.

It was probably even slower if you brought your family. We weren’t able to harvest as much as we planned, maybe the farmer was aiming for that.

“Phew, I’m full!”  

“Kanata said that he’d also come here with Sakura, soon.”  

“At that point, you won’t be able to harvest grapes anymore.”  

“Well, they might wait until spring and go pick strawberries.”

In the end, we had a surprisingly enjoyable time and were in high spirits as we boarded the bus back home.

“…What should we do once we’re back?”  

“Let’s leave the grapes at home for now and then go have lunch outside. Afterwards, we could go to a nearby department store.”

Ending a date after only two hours from 10 am until noon would be a waste, after all. Even so, the grapes might get squished if we took them with us as we walked around.

“Alright! And afterwards?”  

“Afterwards…?”  

“D-Don’t you get my meaning?”

_From her tone of voice, she’s trying to hint at something… Oh, I get it. I still have a long way to go, if it takes me that long._

“After dinner. As Shuu said, minors are officially not allowed in these places, so let’s make sure no one sees us.”  

“Eh-heh-heh, woo-hoo!”

---

**TL notes:**  

I have to apologize for retroactively changing my translation. Back in chapter 594, they jumped from “looking for mushrooms” to “looking for grapes”, which made it sound to me, as if they’d go to the forest and forage for wild grapes. Turns out they were planning to go to something like a vineyard where visitors can gather grapes themselves.

Also, there was an Author’s comment about grapes no longer being harvestable this late in November, but they (again) noticed too late and didn’t want to change everything.

#### Footnotes:

1. In the original, she mishears his Kyohou (巨峰 -> Kyoho grape) for Kyonyuu (巨乳 -> huge breasts). This doesn’t really work in English.[](https://re-library.com/translations/levelmaker/volume-20/chapter-602-grape-picking/#easy-footnote-1-119267)

If the goddess can open the door to the sanctuary, it is proof that she is the real thing, not a proxy. If that's the case, there's no point in doubting a goddess who wants to rule through a contract, and the conclusion is that there's no need to worry about her royal power being shaken. 

"Verdugar is a rich and peaceful country because the labyrinth that brings blessings is in its current form. If it is necessary to maintain it, then there is nothing we can do. I want you to know that I’m looking forward to it.”

"I understand. I'm sure."

 Now……. Now all I have to do is wait for the date for the dinner party.

164 - Sanctuary and monsters

Knight Commander Mildred's attempt was a trial slash, just like last year.

Mildred wields her bastard sword, imbued with fighting spirit, like a stick, and as they pass each other, she splits bamboo and slashes at the trunk, cutting a forest of armor in two as if cutting weeds. 

His skills are as good as ever, but...this year, he's also equipped with aerial combat equipment, and you can see some differences in his ability to kick in the air and change his trajectory to head to the next target. There seems to be a reason why multiple targets were prepared. 

When the banquet ended like that, King Melvin handed out rewards to the knights who had achieved good results. The award was given to Chester, just like last year. Then there's Mercedia. There are a few others.

It seems that there will be a drinking party after this--we are supposed to move to the King's Tower and talk to King Melvin. 

I parted ways with the Marquis and Ophelia and headed to the King's Tower. 

The servant took me to the salon I always use. It was not King Melvin who came, but Mercedia. 

"His Majesty is waiting. First, come here with the young lady who is our guest."

"Okay. Everyone please wait here. I'll be right back."

“Lord Mercedia was also very active at this banquet.”

“It seems like it was worth diving into the labyrinth.However, I still have a long way to go.”

Although he seems humble, he seems quite happy.

Is this the door to the sanctuary? 

"You guys should just go down now."

"Ha!"

Mercedia and the escort knights leave the scene. 

"The dinner party was wonderful."

"No, no, what? It's not me, it's the result of the knights' training. If you tell them those words, they'll be really happy."

“Can you be the goddess Sures?”

"Yes. But first, prove yourself."

Claudia slowly stepped forward and touched the door of the sanctuary in front of King Melvin. 

At that moment, light ran as if tracing a pattern, and the door opened by itself. King Melvin gasped at the sight. That too is temporary. He kneels reverently to Claudia, as his subjects do to their masters. 

"Please stop. I'm not a goddess, I'm just a princess. I'm not worthy of a king bowing down to me."

“No. I believe that you are worthy of being called a goddess, as you have continued to protect this land and the people who live here for a long time.It is also in the words of the ceremony of protection of the country.Protect the country and keep the contract and oath. As long as you continue, you will be recognized as the king of this land. If you and the ancestor of the royal family have signed a contract, there will be no one else but you who can guarantee the royal power of the Verdgar royal family."

Claudia closed her eyes at King Melvin's words. 

"...I understand what you're trying to say. But please keep your head up. I don't like being looked at in that kind of special way."

“That’s what you say, if you will.”

King Melvin stands up. Claudia stepped into the sanctuary. 

"Both of you come here."

Claudia says. ...Will I also enter the sanctuary? Well, it's true that you won't have to worry about paying someone else's attention or being heard by others. 

When the three of us went inside, the place where the door used to be was melted into the wall and disappeared. The sanctuary was a hallway made of stone with a black luster. 

The architectural style itself is close to that of Theorem. However, since not a single seam can be seen in the building materials, it can truly be called a sanctuary. The magical power I feel is also a bit unusual. 

“I would like to thank the Veldgar royal family… especially King Melvin, for keeping the contract with me.”

Claudia says as she goes deeper into the sanctuary. 

"There are some kings who did not fulfill their duties."

King Melvin smiles bitterly. Is this a story about the generation that turned the mine shaft into a labyrinth? 

“Verdogar also has a long history, so that may be the case.”

"If you say so. If you ask me, the goddess... no, Claudia-sama wants to coexist with monsters."

"That's right. Do you know what the difference is between elves and dwarves and those classified as monsters?"

"No, clearly. It's just that some individuals seem to have friendly tendencies."

“What about Theodore?”

When asked, I thought about it for a while. 

That's right. Even if elves and dwarves were sometimes hostile to humans, it was mostly because they couldn't come to terms due to differences in the way of thinking within each race or tribe, or due to personal interests. 

On the other hand, when people like lamias and sirens attack humans, there are times when there is no clear reason to explain it. They are attacked as if there is no need to ask questions. 

“When monsters that are said to have friendly tendencies attack humans, I feel like there are times when there is no clear reason for it.…Well, maybe they just don’t understand the reason. ?”

Claudia nods. 

"First of all, monsters are greatly influenced by the magical power in their surrounding environment."

If there is a pool of magic power, it becomes active and increases in number... or it has the ingredients of a magic stone in its body... There is no doubt that monsters and magic power are closely related. 

“The bottom line is that for the first few years after birth, their personality is determined by the magic of their environment. This is not the case with mature individuals, and some species follow their instincts no matter what the environment is. ”

In short...the way you raise your child in childhood is important. 

"If that's the case...even though it's limited to friendly species, do you think that if the environment is in place you can prevent them from attacking you for no reason?"

"That's right. This goes back to a time when the Kingdom of Verdogar didn't exist yet - that's why I protected the monsters. A magical storm broke out and the monsters went on a rampage, so humans eliminated them. I concluded that it should be done. However... there are many species that become harmless once the disaster has passed... I protected them and hid them in the depths of the labyrinth."

 Really……. In short, Claudia wants him to use this story as a guideline to convince the executives. 

The more friendly monsters are, the higher their intelligence or the more special abilities they have, and the more ferocious they become, the more troublesome they become. 

I can't take countermeasures at first glance, so I often end up being on the defensive until I have more information. If we can completely reduce that risk, this would be a great thing even if we ignore human resources, ethics, and emotional considerations. 

If we're talking about Term Wills, this place will definitely work to pacify the monsters. 

"I see... If you say that's true, then it's true that monsters should be protected. It can reduce the worries of future generations."

Eventually, we arrived at the innermost part of the sanctuary - the hall where the altar was located. A tranquil space illuminated by black stones and vague light. 

However, Claudia passes the altar and continues deeper. When you casually touch the wall, a light flashes and the door opens. 

"this is--"

King Melvin widens his eyes. It seems that King Melvin is following a place he has never been to before. 

“The room ahead is where the management equipment for the Royal Castle Theorem is.”

It was a small hemispherical room. A large crystal-like pillar sits in the center. 

"It's something that the administrator can open and the contractor can operate. It can do things like change the shape of the Royal Castle Theorem..."

King Melvin smiled bitterly as Claudia threw water at him. 

"No, I won't go as far as that. It could cause unnecessary confusion."

“Persuasion, I hope it goes well.”

Claudia came out of the sanctuary and said this to herself without telling anyone. 

"That's right. I feel like I've done what I can, but there's something else..."

After saying that, I had a little idea, so I asked Claudia. 

"--It's a humanization technique. I wonder if it can't be turned into a magic tool?"

"I don't think it's possible... However, depending on your magical ability, you won't be able to maintain the technique for a long time."

"Rather than not being able to use any jutsu at all, I think it would be easier to go out and be accepted by creating one and having people use it."

"Yeah. Let's try it."

Claudia closes her eyes and smiles. 

It's like creating a magic tool with a characteristic seal. It can be used as a source of further support when persuasion does not go well. Let's work together with Claudia and Alfred to move forward with development as soon as possible. 

Now then... I guess what's left is the reward from the treasure trove I promised earlier. When I get back to the salon, I'll arrange for a tour and I'd like you to take a look at the treasure house. Everyone has different hopes, but will they be able to find a bargain?

## 165 - Lion and Goat

“His Majesty has asked me to help you all.”

Take a look around the interior with the woman who is the custodian of the treasure house. An inventory has been made, so if you tell them what you want, they will guide you to the area where the items you want are kept. So it won't be that difficult to find what you're looking for. 

In my case, it's a coat or a robe. This time, I would like to have similar armor for magicians. Grace, who can't wear armor, is going to look for clothes this time as well. 

There were many types, but there was also the issue of size, and the ones that were suitable for practical use were naturally narrowed down. 

What I'm curious about is the black coat... but I feel a strange magical power. When I put the sleeves through, the size changed to match my physique, so it was clearly not an ordinary item. 

“What about this cloak?”

"It's said to be a chimera coat. It's used for self-defense by magicians, and it seems to have magical creatures built into it."

The manager says while looking at the thick catalog. Armor that incorporates magical creatures...Is it something similar to Ouroboros? It looks normal so far... 

"It seems that the wielder can move magical creatures by supplying magical power."

says the administrator. 

“Can I call you for a while?”

"please"

I received permission, so I tried passing magic through the coat...and the shoulders swelled up, and the heads of a black lion and a black goat popped out. The manager took a step back with a twitchy smile at the sight. 

"This again..."

It seems that the lion can not only put out its head but also its front paws with sharp claws. These animals can change their appearance position to some extent, not only from the shoulder, but also from the sleeve or hem. 

 I see. It's a chimera. It seems that it moves by supplying magical power, and that it listens to my wishes and protects me in close combat. 

They say it's for self-defense, but since it can unleash attacks with lion's fangs and claws, I think it's also effective as an offensive weapon. It will simply increase the amount of work involved. 

Because they are magical creatures, they follow orders and move autonomously to some extent. As long as you wear it, you can control it completely and move it like a limb. 

“What about the goat head?”

"In addition to headbutting with the horns, it seems that you can also exhale. It seems that the wielder needs to supply magical power."

"...It would have been perfect if there was also a snake."

Well, that role will be left to Ouroboros. That one is a dragon though. 

For now... unlike a wand, it's not a magic activator, so there doesn't seem to be any worry about it putting a load on the magic circulation. And it can be incorporated into the magic circulation. In short, the reinforcement means that you can ride a lion or a goat... I won't know until I actually try it. 

"What can I say...it's interesting."

You can think of combinations with a lion or a goat, or you can leave your hand face down to cause a surprise attack... conversely, it will also prevent the wearer from being surprised. 

“Furthermore, since it is a magical creature, even if the cloak gets damaged, it can repair itself.”

It will match the size...and it will also require enchantment. Plus, it's self-healing. Isn't this a lifelong thing if you don't do it right? 

"Hmm. I'll decide on this."

## 175 - Unveiling

Hmm. Evilweed, which has been rendered harmless, is surprisingly charming and may be suitable as a houseplant. Evilweed, which grew accustomed to humans through water magic, has become too obedient, and I feel that it has moved away from its original purpose of being used as a guard dog. 

Well, since thieves don't know whether they are harmless or harmful, they could just put them in large numbers to show off...but that's a bit...

“Hmm….Did you also make a flower bed?”

"No. Especially for me. I feel like it would have happened naturally if I had left Evil Weed there."

Ashley tilts her head. 

“Perhaps it will be easier for plants to grow around Evilweed.”

"I don't know. It's true that wild evilweed tends to prefer deep bushes, but..."

If you think about it, these guys can't move on their own. It is possible that they choose such a place arbitrarily because they scatter the seeds...or do they prepare the surrounding environment? 

"There may be other factors as well... so let's give it a try."

“What are you going to do?”

"Plant them together with other plants. See if the presence or absence of evilweed makes a difference in the growth of the plants you plant together."

Check the garden for plants whose buds have not yet opened, and move them into pots to create groups that coexist with evilweed and groups that stand alone. Then I placed it a little further away. 

They get about the same amount of sunlight, so...well, it's probably a reasonable place to group them. 

The relocated Evil Weeds were showing a gesture of staring intently at their roommate, who had not yet bloomed. 

If this goes well, you might be able to see the effect of making the flowers last longer by placing them together with other plants in a bay window or the like. 

For a long time, they were treated as enemies of gardeners, but if you get used to them, they might become your allies in gardening. 

In a more advanced form... if it can exterminate pests that eat away at crops and deal with pathogens... then it will be a great ally for agriculture. Maybe I'm expecting too much, but it's worth checking out.

## What, Failure to Transition!? - Volume 9 - ### Chapter 7 – Akaho Co., Ltd

After the arrangements were complete, the two headed over to the hotel where Yoichi is staying for the meeting.

“Seriously, you came along pretty easily—” Yoichi remarked immediately after their arrival.

“—After all that attempts in escaping using smoke bombs and complaining about not wanting to be in enemy territory and such.”

Of course, that snide remark was not left unattended by Jiang Chengxi, whose real name was Zhu Xihan.

“Whaat!? After you dumped a load inside me like that, you gonna act like we’re strangers now? Yangyi and I, we’re partners now. So your place is my place now, right?”

“If you’re okay with that, I guess.”

“Welcome back, Yoichi. And welcome too, this land’s infamous phantom thief.”

Naturally, Karin was informed beforehand, so she was able to welcome them with a warm smile.

Xihan, however, wasn’t.

“Aiyaa! Such a beautiful wife, and Yangyi still comes to my place all alone?” She exclaimed as soon as she stepped inside, playing it up.

“Hey, lay off, will ya…”

“We aren’t married yet, just you know,” Karin interjected.

“Not yet, huh? So, maybe you will get married?”

“Who knows?” Karin replied to Xihan, a mischievous glint in her eye as she turned it on Yoichi.

“Yeah, ha ha…” but Yoichi could only manage a sheepish grin, scratching the back of his neck.

“Hey, Yangyi? About earlier…”

Thinking about where she should begin, Xihan started to whisper in his ear, but Yoichi, as if he knew her reluctance, waved his hand away, signalling it doesn’t matter.

“Don’t worry, she’s part of this. I’ve also told Karin everything.”

“Really?! You told her everything? Like how you shot one load in my mouth and filled my pussy five times over? You told her all that?!”

“Hey, you don’t have to tell her all that!”

“Well, it’s Yoichi. What can you expect?”

“Aiyaa! And you just accepted that, miss? That means Yangyi’s a real lady-killer, huh? Doesn’t look like it!”

“Oh shut it,” Yoichi grumbled.

After a playful banter, the three of them settled onto the sofa in the living room.

“Still, it’s an honor to meet the legendary thief Jiang Chengxi in person,” Karin began.

“You know about her, Karin?” Yoichi asked, surprised.

“Yeah. She’s been all over the news, talk shows, the works.”

“Ahaha, you’re making me blush!” Xihan then exclaimed, scratching her head as if genuinely embarrassed.

Karin just smiled and extended a hand towards her.

“Alright, shall we begin the introductions? I’m Karin. Though, some people around here just call me Huali.”1

“Then I shall call you Huali as well. As you know, I am the legendary phantom thief, Jiang Chengxi. But you can call me Xihan.”

“What does Yoichi call you?”

“Xihan.”

“Then Xihan it is.”

“Sounds good to me.”

The two women then shook hands.

“Alright, let me lay out the situation for you both.”

Yoichi restarted the conversation, launching into an explanation.

The sword that they needed as reference for Alex’s weapon, as he explained, was already in the hands of Huang Lao, Xihan’s client.

To meet with Huang Lao (and get the sword), they would need some kind of offering. And Yoichi’s plan was to use stolen artwork currently held by Akaho Co., Ltd as that very gift.

“So that’s the gist of it… What’s wrong, Karin? You’ve got a real serious look on your face.”

“Hey Yoichi… Akaho… is that like, how do you spell it… red (赤 – aka) and then ‘ear of rice’ (穂 – ho) making it Akaho?”

“Yeah, why? You know it?”

“Is that…related to Ako Health Foods?”

“Uh… yeah, it is. “Ako Health Foods” is the parent company, and “Akaho Co., Ltd” is their overseas branch.”

“I thought it was unusual to pronounce it “Akaho” instead of “Ako” when it’s written with ‘red’ and ‘ear of rice,’ but I guess that makes sense…”

Karin let out a heavy sigh.

“What’s wrong?”

Yoichi asked, concern in his voice.

“‘Does that company happen to employ someone named Hongou Souichi?’”

“Uh, let me check… Yeah… It does… wait, wasn’t he…?”

“Yeah, he’s the junior colleague I was telling you about the other day.”

“No way…” Yoichi’s eyes widened. “He’s in this branch.”

“…Seriously?” Karin’s voice was barely a whisper.

“Yeah. And what’s more, he’s top guy in the entire branch.”

“Aiyaa, it’s a small world, isn’t it?”

Xihan, who was listening to the side the entire time, spoke the last line, though it was almost an interjection.

A mischievous glint sparked in her eyes, a stark contrast to her surprised tone.

She must be thinking that if the head of Akaho in this town is an acquaintance, it would be more convenient for them.

But Karin had other ideas.

“Hey, wasn’t Akaho supposed to be…?” she began hesitantly, a knot of anxiety tightening in her stomach.

“…a front for organized crime,” yet Yoichi still finished, despite the words leaving his mouth with a reluctant air.

“What is he even doing…?”

As if she wasn’t expecting this terrible news, Karin pressed her fingers to her forehead and shook her head.

She was utterly exasperated on how to convey the situation to the troublesome former colleague about what he has gotten into.

〇●〇●

Karin sat alone at an outdoor cafe, sipping her coffee.

The cafe was conveniently located halfway between the hotel where Yoichi and the others were staying, and the building owned by Ako.

After a few minutes, a man approached her table.

“Sorry, sorry I’m late!”

It was Hongou Souichi, and he slid into the seat opposite Karin, his voice filled with brightness despite his apology.

“No worries, I haven’t been waiting long.”

“That’s good to hear.”

After mopping his brow with a handkerchief, he signaled a passing waitress.

“Iced latte, please. Still, this is incredible. I can’t believe I’m running into you here, Miss Motomiya.”

He began as soon as he ordered, a touch of forced surprise in his tone.

“Tell me about it,” Karin responded dryly.

After a few polite pleasantries, Souichi’s expression turned serious. He leaned forward slightly.

“So, about the thing we discussed… is it true?” he asked, lowering his voice.

Karin met his gaze, her own face hardening. Then she gave a curt nod.

“We’ve been trying to get an introduction to Huang Lao for ages, so this is perfect… but how did you get involved, Miss Motomiya?”

“Oh, you know, it’s a friend of a friend kind of thing. Huang Lao wants to build a good relationship with Akaho too, so it’s a win-win situation.”

They spent some time going over the specifics of the meeting, and then agreed to call it a day.

Souichi asked as Karin started to rise.

“Would you want to drop by our office, Miss Motomiya?”

“No way. I told you before, didn’t I?”

“But…”

“Actually, let me ask you something. Did it ever cross your mind to leave Akaho, Mr. Hongou?”

“Leave Akaho? Why would I?”

“Why would you not…?” Karin’s voice trailed off.

Despite her lack of affection for him, she couldn’t deny they were once colleagues.

The idea of a former coworker being involved with unsavory characters troubled her, at least a little.

“Akaho might be nothing back in Japan, but it’s a huge deal here! Our income is on a whole different level than before, we’ve got connections! We can get practically anything we want! So, quit Akaho?! No way!”

Souichi continued, oblivious to her inner conflict, pride practically radiating off him.

“Then again, why are you still with that guy, Miss Motomiya? Meeting with Huang Lao means this isn’t just a vacation, right? So why is _he_ tagging along?”

“…So you knew I was here with him all along.”

“I told you, things like that are easy to find out.”

“I figured you wouldn’t bother since I turned you down the other day.”

“I just like to be prepared in case you change your mind.”

Karin’s brow furrowed, a flicker of distaste crossing her face, but Souichi missed it entirely.

“So, are you thinking of staying here? If you are, you should send that guy packing.”

“Definitely not. I’ll go back once I’m done here. With him, of course.”

“But you’ve got a connection with Huang Lao! And you’re connected with me now! Why? It’s gotta be better here than back in Japan! You’d be way happier with me than with that loser!”

“Sigh… So, that’s a no on quitting, then.”

“Not even a question! Anyway, you were saying…”

“My bad,” Karin interrupted, a hint of regret in her voice.

She’d said more than she intended to.

Further conversation would likely lead nowhere, and potentially complicate her plans. So she decided to cut things short.

“I shouldn’t have brought it up. See you then.”

“…Ah. Yeah, see you,” Souichi replied, a little flustered, finally realizing he might have overstepped.

He watched Karin walk away, a slightly bewildered expression on his face.

〇●〇●

The Scarlet Spica Hotel, a gleaming monument to luxury, was the crown jewel in the Akaho Co., Ltd portfolio.

Its sister establishments graced the skylines of coastal metropolises, bustling capitals, and other sprawling urban centers.

Now, a relatively short time ago, this inland city had been deemed worthy of its own Scarlet Spica.

The lower levels housed a sprawling department store, a veritable shopper’s paradise.

Above that, soaring into the heavens, rose the hotel itself.

And on its very highest floor, in the most opulent of its suites, the entire Akaho brass was present and accounted for, a constellation of sharp suits and concerned whispers.

“Thank you for accepting our invitation today, and welcome to our humble city.”

The voice, smooth and resonant despite its age, belonged to a distinguished gentleman standing on a small stage at the far end of the room.

He held a glass of something amber in his hand, the light catching the slicked-back waves of his thick white hair.

This was Huang Lao, or as his birth certificate might have read, Tanaka Shokichi.

His lineage, as the name suggested, was deeply entwined with Japan.

He was one of the so-called “left-behind children,” a product of a tumultuous era.2

Against all odds, he had not only survived but thrived, becoming an indispensable figure in the current government.

In a nation where the changing of the management often triggered a brutal wave of purges, Huang Lao had maintained his esteemed position at the central level for over half a century.

This remarkable feat was attributed almost entirely to his influential connections within Japanese high society.

Though the nation projected an image of hegemonic power, flexing its military might with a seemingly arrogant disregard for others, the importance of its backchannels to foreign dignitaries could not be overstated.

“The pleasure is all ours, Huang Lao,” replied Souichi, standing beside the elder statesman on the stage.

“As people who share common roots, we consider it a profound honor to host you,” he also added while offering a respectful bow.

Despite having officially stepped back from the front lines, Huang Lao still wielded considerable influence within the country.

As such, for Akaho Co., Ltd, a company with little existing leverage in these circles, securing his favor was a high priority.

That’s why when Karin had proposed this meeting, Souichi had seized the opportunity without hesitation.

Across the crowded venue, near a wall draped in heavy brocade, Yoichi watched the staged exchange alongside Xihan.

He wore the crisp black waiter uniform of the hotel staff, a borrowed guise for their clandestine purpose.

Xihan, as elegant as ever, was resplendent in the same lilac cheongsam he had seen her in before.

“You know,” Yoichi muttered, his voice low, “now that we have come here and all, can’t we just go to him directly?”

Yoichi’s sole objective was to meet Huang Lao and retrieve the katana.

Xihan, however, had been adamant that such an audience wouldn’t be granted easily.

She’d stressed the necessity of a “proper offering” before even attempting an introduction.

And now, here was the man himself, their target, just a stone’s throw away.

It felt absurdly convoluted to Yoichi.

Meanwhile, as if she had noticed his inner turmoil, Xihan’s gaze flickered to him, a hint of amusement playing on her lips

“Let me put it in this way. This is also a question of whether you bring the other guy onto your turf or venture into theirs. In the end, it depends on who thinks they have more to lose.”

Yoichi’s brow furrowed with confusion as he watched the exchange unfold.

“…So, you mean Huang Lao didn’t want me to come to his place?”

But instead of giving a reply, Xihan gently cupped Yoichi’s chin instead, turning his face away from the stage and directing it towards her.

“Hey!”

Yoichi was of course startled, a touch of annoyance in his voice at the forced redirection.

But as he met her gaze, the tension within him seemed to dissipate.

There, Xihan continued.

“At the very least, you mustn’t arrive empty-handed. Didn’t I tell you that multiple times?”

Her smile was knowing, a subtle curve that hinted at secrets and understanding.

Yet her voice, when she spoke, held a patient, almost maternal tone.

“…Guess you did.”

Yoichi finally conceded, a reluctant acknowledgment in his voice.

“Yes, I did,” to which Xihan affirmed softly, finally releasing his chin.

Yoichi turned back to the stage.

Expression still somewhat bemused, he stared at Huang Lao, a faint nod of comprehension slowly forming.

The old man’s every gesture and word spoke of power, carefully measured and deliberately displayed.

Perhaps, Yoichi mused, there was more to this dance of diplomacy than he initially understood.

“Nfufufu, that’s it, good boy, doing exactly as he’s told.”

With a nasty little twist tugging at the corner of her mouth, Xihan mused, but just as quickly, she smoothed out into a more approachable smile.

“Still, you have to hand it to Huali. She really pulled this off.”

Yoichi, who had been staring vacantly into the middle distance, blinked back to awareness when he heard.

“Well, Karin is capable. You know that.”

The government here wasn’t keen on Huang Lao getting too cozy with Japanese companies.

So, Karin had come up with the idea – how to get Huang Lao and the Akaho bigwigs together without setting off any government alarm bells.

Souichi, ever the opportunist, had jumped on it, suggesting this hotel as the perfect neutral ground.

“So the whole deception, i mean the cover-up, is it airtight then?”

Xihan asked, this time her eyes as sharp as blades.

“Of course.” Yoichi nodded, unfazed.

From the blueprint stage onward, they’d greased the wheels, ensuring the system could be fooled, events within the hotel masked or outright erased.”

As proof, in this packed venue which was bustling with a hundred or so guests—a carefully orchestrated chaos—the security cameras were broadcasting footage of empty hallways being scrubbed down.

“Also, as far as Hongou’s concerned, Karin’s just another Japanese businesswoman to him. They probably think she’s just an innocent soul they managed to lure right into their home territory.”

Yoichi chuckled.

Watching Souichi hold court with a beaming Huang Lao on the stage, he couldn’t help but suppress his laughter.

Only then was Xihan finally content.

“Alright, well, I’m off then. You’re absolutely sure you’ve got everything else covered?”

Before leaving, she asked one last time, a touch of theatrical concern in her voice.

“Yeah, no problem.”

“…Though, where did you even dig up such a knockout?”

Xihan’s gaze flickered towards the stage.

“That’s a secret. Now, now, your cue’s coming up.”

Toward the shooing Yoichi, Xihan waved a dismissive hand, already turning away.

[Now, from our side—]

[—we will present a truly exquisite vintage in this gathering.]

A murmur of surprise, then appreciative whistles, rippled through the venue.

The reaction wasn’t really about the aged Shaoxing wine they carried, but about the women themselves.

And standing center stage, impossible to ignore, was a woman with hair the color of spun moonlight.

Her dress, a blush of pale rose, seemed to take inspiration from the traditional Hanfu, the sleeves wide and flowing like the wings of a bird.

But there the demureness ended.

The hemline was daringly short, barely concealing the impressive curve of her breasts.

And if that wasn’t enough, a vertical slit ran up the center, offering a tantalizing glimpse of the shadowed valley between.

From the swell of her underbust to the bare expanse of her navel, she was a captivating display.

Her skin was smooth and luminous, like polished porcelain.

Even the deep slits in her skirt, revealing long stretches of leg, couldn’t diminish the air of regal grace that clung to her.

She was a vision, a mythical being descended into the modern world, and every man in the room was utterly captivated.

The woman was none other than Alana.

Beside her, there was also Misato, in a more understated but equally striking cheongsam.

Hers was white, trimmed with delicate blue embroidery, lending her an air of quiet elegance.

The sleeves barely covered her shoulders, and the hem stopped a good six inches above her knees, showcasing her slender limbs.

She was seated near the stage, resplendent in a black, sleeveless dress slashed with red – the very same dress she’d worn back in that casino town.

The slit up her thigh was even higher this time, threatening to reveal far more than just her leg.

(Hope you know what you’re doing…)

“Easy there, pal,” Yoichi said dismissively.

“That’s… that’s just a toy! You think you can scare me with that—!”

Thwack!

“Eep!”

Even muffled by the silencer, the gunshot was sharp and loud. Souichi let out a strangled yelp.

The bullet ripped a charred hole in the expensive carpet and embedded itself in the floorboards with a dull thud.

“That’s… that’s…”

The color drained from Souichi’s face.

Yoichi’s weapon was real.

He flinched as the cold steel pressed back against his skin.

But then, as if a thought struck him, his gaze darted around the room, locking onto Karin’s figure.

Her voice held an apologetic tone, but her expression was anything but remorseful.

“No… way…”

Stunned by her words, Souichi could only stare.

At the end, he could only clench his teeth, his fury shifting back to Yoichi.

“You! You put her up to this!”

“You’re an idiot, aren’t ya?”

Yoichi sighed, rolling his eyes at his reaction.

“Do you really believe that Karin is the kind of woman who’d do something like this just because I told her to?”

“Oh, but I’d do anything for you, Yoichi.”

But as if having fun for some reason, Karin immediately purred beside.

“Hey, this is not the time for that,” to which Yoichi muttered back to her in admonishment.

It was a scene so sweet that even Alana, who was still holding Souichi firm, and Misato, who was cautiously scanning the surroundings, couldn’t suppress small smiles.

The search for Yangyi and the other guy had probably begun.
