Souichi couldn’t exactly confess that he’d been robbed, so he didn’t press the issue further.

And so, the party at the Scarlet Spica Hotel, hosted by Huang Lao, drew to a close, outwardly appearing to have been a smooth success.

### Translator Notes:

1. Karin and Huaili. Again, this is one of those Kanji Characters (alphabet the Japanese “borrowed” from the Chinese) being pronounced by their native Chinese origins, and the name Karin (花Ka梨Rin) is pronounced as Huali (花Hua梨Li) in Chinese.

Intrestingly, Karin (assuming the same character spelling) means Flower(花) and pear(梨) and together in Japanese they are a type of fruit called quince, which is the hard, aromatic fruit that comes from a small tree or shrub of the Rose family.

![](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/01/karin-fruit-1.jpg?w=480)

Karin Fruit (Quince)

![](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/01/karin-fruit-2.jpg?w=480)

Karin Fruit (Quince) Sliced

As for the Chinese one, well, I don’t know if this is correct, but Google only translates it to the (Chinese) Rosewood, a luxury material for woodworking and is valued for its rich amber tones and abstract figural patterns, including the famed darker cluster markings called “ghostmarks”.

![](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/01/rosewood-furniture.jpg?w=320)

Rosewood Furniture

![](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/01/rosewood-with-ghostmark2.jpg?w=747)

Rosewood with Ghostmark 1

![](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/01/rosewood-with-ghostmark1.jpg?w=744)

Rosewood with Ghostmark 2

It is now classified as “vulnerable” species and only a speck away from being “endangered” due to illegal logging and exploitation. Again, I don’t know if the Chinese one refers to the wood, or the fruit as well.[↰](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/stabbingwithasyringe-translated-works/what-failure-to-transition-success/what-failure-to-transition-volume-9-chapter-7/#subscript1)

2.  “Left-behind Children” or 残留孤児. AS the wiki says, they are Japanese who were unable to return to Japan due to the sudden Soviet invasion and the withdrawal of the Kwantung Army at the end of World War II and remained stranded in mainland China. Under Japanese law, they are also called Japanese nationals residing in China, and sometimes referred to as “Left-behind Children in China” when limited to orphans.

But before we get to that, let me explain the Kwantung Army first. The Kwantung Army is to sum up, a security force that expanded into an army group during the Interwar period to support Japanese interests in China, Manchuria, and Mongolia. During that period, the Kwantung Army became the most prestigious command in the Imperial Japanese Army, and many of its personnel won promotions to high positions in the Japanese military and civil government. It is also one of the sponsors of one of the most horrible warcrime groups on earth’s history – the Unit 731.

Still, despite the war crimes committed (which was of course, hidden at that time), it invited Japanese seeking better opportunities, so many migrated for work over there. It didn’t help that at that time is also the Showa Depression (which was also caused by the Great Depression in the US) so many people were inclined to work overseas despite the country’s extreme nationalistic values.

That’s why when the Soviets abrogated the neutrality pact it had concluded with Japan, and declared war on them in surprise, many Japanese in Manchuria were unable to react in time. Sure, the Kwantung Army became one of the biggest forces that played the role in WW2, but that’s because the Imperialists prioritized the army’s logistics over everything. Because of that, when the surprise attack came, to avoid further turmoil, the Kwantung Army only informed the citizens of the attack the day after, when the families of the military have already escaped. It didn’t help that the Kwantung Army also requisitioned trucks and cars from the civilians and also secured the trains beforehand for a fast withdrawal, leaving the citizens barefoot and stranded as the Soviets attacked.

Having nothing left for them, and with the army’s withdrawal, law and order became nonexistent, and many lives were lost when the winter came. Lucky young ones survived when they are adopted by Chinese families whether through familial ties or human trafficking. This is where the term “Left-behind Children” came from, while the women survived by becoming “Left-behind wives” by straight up selling themselves just to avoid starvation. The adult men were drafted to form a “Border Patrol Force” to confront the invading Soviet Army.[↰](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/stabbingwithasyringe-translated-works/what-failure-to-transition-success/what-failure-to-transition-volume-9-chapter-7/#subscript2)

“Sigh… and here I am, falling for a guy who’s seriously something else.”

Looking around at the room that was now reasonably tidy, as if the earlier chaos was a lie, Xihan muttered in a self-deprecating, yet entranced tone.

“Wait. Xihan, you have seriously fallen for me?”

“Huh? What was that for? After what you’ve done, of course I am!”

Xihan raised an eyebrow for a moment, but immediately softened her expression, a seductive smile playing on her lips as she approached Yoichi.

“You’re the first man who hasn’t fallen for my bedroom techniques after all.”

Then, she wrapped her arms and legs around him, clinging to him from the front, and looked up at Yoichi with upturned eyes.

“You made me beg and plead for you that much… you’ll take responsibility for that, right…?”

“Um… responsibility, you mean…?”

Right now, his heart is pounding in various ways even more so as Xihan’s face slowly drew closer, but Yoichi still managed to ask.

“When a man takes responsibility for a woman, there’s only one thing it means, right…?”

Just as their noses were about to touch, Xihan’s face shifted slightly to the side.

Then, getting so close to Yoichi’s ear that her lips might have touched it, she whispered softly.

“So include me in Yangyi’s harem too, okay?”

“Hah? Harem…?”

“Ahahaha…!”

Xihan laughed, teasing Yoichi’s surprise, and stepped back lightly.

“H-hey… what’s with the harem?”

“Nihih, it just means let’s all get along in the future☆”

Saying that, Xihan turned her back to Yoichi and looked around the room again.

“Hmm, it seems it can’t be completely restored.”

“Huh? Oh, yeah… that’s true…”

Slightly bewildered by the sudden change in topic, Yoichi breathed a sigh of relief.

“Well, they probably stole some things while they were trashing the place.”

About 80% of the ransacked room had been restored, so he decided to pay extra money to resolve the rest.

“Well then, I’m going to call grandpa.”

A few days later, Yoichi and the others were to meet with Huang Lao.

〇●〇●

Huang Lao’s residence was located in a corner of a very ordinary office building, a little way from the city center of an inland metropolis.

Though it was just one of his residences and bases scattered in various locations.

“Welcome. I bid you welcome.”

Yoichi and the others were invited into a Japanese-style room with a surprisingly calm atmosphere, quite unlike what the building’s exterior suggested.

“Thank you very much for inviting us.”

As Yoichi said this and bowed his head, beside him were not only Karin, but also Alana and Misato.

Naturally, Xihan was standing next to Huang Lao.

The women were dressed in the same dresses and suits they wore at the party held at the Scarlet Spica Hotel the other day.

For reference, Yoichi was in a tweed three-piece suit.

“Come, sit down. How about we start with a toast, shall we?”

On the low table, a furniture common in traditional Japanese households, some light dishes were already arranged.

On the center, a familiar earthenware jar of Shaoxing wine was placed.

It was the same Shaoxing wine that was distributed in the gathering.

“Um, before we toast, there’s something I’d like to ask.”

“And what might that be?”

“Why did you invite them?”

While asking Huang Lao, Yoichi looked at Alana and Misato.

When considering visiting Huang Lao, he had hoped to bring at least Alana along and was wondering how to justify it. Then, unexpectedly, he received this offer.

It was convenient for Yoichi, but it made him curious about the reason.

“Well, I saw them at the venue the other day and thought I’d very much like them to pour me a drink. Unfortunately, by the time I’d noticed, they were gone.”

“Is that how it was?”

Alana, receiving Yoichi’s gaze again, smiled and nodded, and started to rise.

“Ah, no need to trouble yourself, from there is fine.”

But Huang Lao stopped her.

Yoichi and the four others were sitting facing Huang Lao, so Alana had thought that to pour a drink, she should go next to him and was about to stand up.

Xihan nodded beside Huang Lao, so Alana knelt down to reach the low table and pulled the earthenware jar containing the wine towards her.

Then, she scooped some of the contents with a ladle and poured it into Huang Lao’s glass.

“Well then, to good fortune on this day, cheers.”

After everyone’s glasses were filled, they raised their cups and toasted.

After that, aimless small talk continued.

“Now then, I hear there’s an ‘offering’?”

At that moment, a man in black clothes entered the room.

His movements were calm, but his expression was stiff.

“What is it?”

“Actually…”

The man whispered in Huang Lao’s ear.

“Hmm… men from Akaho? But this place shouldn’t be somewhere those kinds of people can easily get into.”

This building, which looked like just an ordinary office building, had very strict security, as it was one of Huang Lao’s bases.

“That is…”

The man in black looked at Xihan with a troubled expression.

“Sorry, Grandpa, I asked them to lower the security level on our instructions.”

“…What did you say?”

The words were spoken in a quiet tone, but they seemed to weigh heavily on Xihan, who shrank back like a scolded kitten.

“Sorry, I asked her to.”

“Oh?”

His gaze was sharp.

Indeed, one could fully feel the dignity of someone who had lived through the turbulent times from the postwar era to the present day.

However, it was only a few decades.

Compared to Celestin, who had lived for hundreds of years and protected the frontier from hordes of monsters for over a hundred years, this was not much of an opponent.

“The other day, there was an incident at the Scarlet Spica Hotel where a large amount of artwork disappeared, you see. It seems the Akaho group has learned that those artworks are here, and the culprits who stole them are here today.”

Huang Lao slightly furrowed his brow at Yoichi, who spoke without flinching from his piercing gaze.

“Could it be that your so-called ‘offering’ is…?”

“Yes, it’s those artworks.”

“So, you stole them then?”

“We just took back stolen goods, though.”

“You—!”

The man in black clothes, enraged by Yoichi’s words and attitude, looked like he was about to lunge, but Huang Lao lightly raised his hand to restrain him.

Then he shifted his gaze to Xihan.

“Xihan, did you use me as bait?”

“…Grandpa, I’m sorry.”

Xihan, remaining huddled, hung her head.

“I see, Xihan used me… is that it…”

Huang Lao, blinking as he looked at the shrinking Xihan, suddenly relaxed his expression.

“Very well. Xihan, do as you please.”

“Huang Lao!?”

“Grandpa!”

The man in black and Xihan shouted at the same time.

“Yangyi, was it?”

Huang Lao looked at Yoichi again.

His gaze no longer held the sharpness from before.

“Is it alright if you take point?”

“Yes.”

“Then, I shall leave it to you.”

From Huang Lao’s expression, it was clear that he was genuinely entrusting the situation to Yoichi.

The man in black clothes tried to protest, but then closed his mouth as if giving up.

“Okay, Misato and Xihan, you’re Huang Lao’s bodyguards.”

“Yes.”

“Leave it to me! I won’t let a finger touch Grandpa!!”

“Karin and Alana, you’re with me for interception then.”

“Okay.”

“Understood.”

“And, Mr. Black Suit, could you arrange for your people to not interfere? We’ll take care of everything.”

“Hmph…”

The man in black glared at Yoichi with a disgruntled expression, but upon receiving Huang Lao’s gaze, he silently nodded and left the room.

“Alright then, let’s wrap this up quickly.”

〇●〇●

The enemy moved in small groups and entered the target building.

The surveillance cameras around the building were unavoidable, but since they had mostly managed to subdue the building’s security, they posed no problem.

They switched the footage from the entrance and hallways to recordings that showed everything was normal, and had their infiltrated personnel stand by inside the building.

“Hmph, if I really wanted to, even I can do something like this.”

The camera hacking went surprisingly well, and to top it off, the office on the same floor as Huang Lao was, supposedly, closed for temporary business and completely empty.

Souichi thought, _Luck is on my side._

“Heh heh… I can’t wait to see the look on their faces.”

Over a hundred personnel were already on standby in the office.

They knew Yoichi and the others would be there that day, but the only thing they hadn’t been able to figure out was where the artworks were being stored.

If they had known that, it would have been possible to secretly steal just the artworks.

“Well, not that I was planning to let them off that easily.”

But either way, Souichi probably wouldn’t have changed his plan.

_‘Now let me ask you this time. Could you have gotten a warehouse-worth of stolen artworks back in a blink of an eye, Mr. Hongou?’_ Karin’s words replayed over and over in Souichi’s mind.

“There’s not a single thing that guy can do that I can’t.”

In the end, they still hadn’t figured out what method Yoichi had used to steal back the stolen goods and escape their grasp.

But for Souichi, that was irrelevant now.

“Everyone, are you ready?”

He looked at the assembled personnel.

Some were in suits, others in casual clothes.

This was to deceive surveillance on their way here and blend in with the general public.

However, their expressions were serious.

They weren’t just any thugs; they were trained members.

And there were over a hundred of them.

He felt they were dependable.

And even proud.

This was the power that Souichi had spent years acquiring.

“I’ll show them what’s what.”

He put his hand on the door.

“Let’s go.”

Confirming that everyone silently nodded, Souichi opened the door.

It was a long, single corridor leading to the room where Huang Lao and the others were.

The locks of the several offices along the way had been tampered with to prevent them from opening.

Of course, access to this floor via the emergency stairs and elevators had also been disabled.

Even if Huang Lao had guards, there would be at most ten or so.

Subduing them would be easy.

“Heh heh heh…”

Souichi let out a dark chuckle, a nightstick clutched in his hand as he walked at the front.

The other members’ weapons were also mainly blunt instruments or bare hands; they weren’t carrying blades or firearms.

“I’m not going to kill you… I don’t intend to kill you, though.”

They would capture everyone.

If they resisted, they would be beaten.

They would subdue them with overwhelming numbers.

That was all there was to it.

They could extract the location of the hidden art pieces through torture or whatever else it took.

The door at the end of the corridor opened.

“Oh my, a welcoming committee, how kind of you.”

Yoichi was the first to appear, followed by Alana and Karin.

“Huh, so that woman is here too.”

Souichi slightly raised an eyebrow as he looked at Alana.

“The woman is free for you guys to do as you like. However, I’ll deal with Motomiya first myself.”

When Souichi said that, lewd laughter erupted from the members.

Perhaps they were complacent due to their numerical advantage.

And it seemed they were also confident that their victory was assured, no matter how complacent they were.

Suppressing his eagerness, Souichi walked forward leisurely.

He thought that slowly, deliberately approaching would increase their despair.

“Hmph, so you intend to resist, huh?”

Yoichi remained unarmed and lowered his stance.

Alana was holding batons in both hands – dual wielding, which seemed amateurish to him.

And then there was Karin—

“A bow!?”

Seeing Karin poised with a compound bow, Souichi couldn’t help but burst out laughing.

Come to think of it, he had heard a story that she had done archery in her student days.

He found it comical that, after desperately thinking of ways to resist, she had desperately resorted to using a bow.

“But if you’re going to use projectile weapons, I guess I have no choice.”

Smiling sinisterly as he watched Karin draw her bow, Souichi reached into his jacket.

He had prepared a handgun just for himself, unlike the other members.

“Sorry if my aim is off.”

A bow, such an antiquated weapon, was no match for a gun.

So thought Souichi as he gripped the gun and started to pull it from its holster.

— _Whoosh!_

In that instant, just as he heard a sharp sound like the wind being cut, Souichi felt a strong impact on his shoulder.

〇●〇●

Opening the door and leaving Huang Lao’s room, they were confronted by over a hundred men, led by Souichi, who were bearing down on them.

Even looking at Yoichi and the others, they were walking slowly – probably intending it as intimidation.

“Compared to a rampaging horde of monsters, they’re more like a flock of ducklings, aren’t they?”

“Oh, but I really don’t want to shoot arrows at a flock of ducklings?”

“A flock of ducklings, huh? I saw a video of them, and they’re quite nice.”

There wasn’t a shred of tension between the three of them.

[You can do whatever you want with the women. But Motomiya is mine first.] Souichi’s voice reached them.

Normally, this distance would be barely audible, but the three of them here have sharpened senses due to skills and such.

“Honestly, he’s hopeless, isn’t he?”

Utterly exasperated, Karin nocked an arrow on her bow.

It was fitted with a rubber bullet instead of an arrowhead – something with low killing power.

Souichi, wearing a vulgar expression she’d never seen when they were at the same company, was mercilessly targeted.

He started saying something and reached into his jacket, but Karin was not about to give him time to pull it out.

—_Whoosh!_

“Gah!?”

The arrow, cutting through the air, struck Souichi’s right shoulder.

The force of the impact made Souichi reel back, his hand was pulled from inside his jacket, but he dropped the handgun he was holding right there.

Even though it has a rubber tip, it was still an arrow fired from a powerful bow at a relatively close range.

His bone probably shattered.

“Haaah!”

“Oraah!!”

Alana and Yoichi rushed into the group.

Karin supported them from the rear, firing arrows to cover them.

Swinging batons in both hands, Alana leaped into the midst of the waiting members.

Every time she swung her arms, the long sleeves of her dress fluttered.

“Gweh!?”

“Gyah…!”

“Wha, you bast- guah!!”

Alana’s movements were like a refined dance, but each graceful flutter of her dress was accompanied by gruff screams, and men fell one after another.

They didn’t seem to have the leeway to appreciate the voluptuous breasts peeking out and swaying from below Alana’s cheongsam.

These were men who had been involved in various crimes until now.

Knowing this perhaps, Alana relentlessly swung her batons, crushing the bones of the men’s faces, arms, shoulders, collarbones, thighs, and knees.

“Such a weak amateur punch—goboh…!!”

On the other side, Yoichi’s short uppercut landed squarely on the man’s stomach.

At first glance, he looked flimsy, maybe at most lean and muscular to some extent.

However, Yoichi’s attack, boasting strength beyond his appearance due to the [Healthy Body α] effect, was fast and heavy.

After all, he now possessed the muscle strength to swing a knife weighing over 100 kilos with ease.

His attack power was not just heavy-class, but more like heavy machinery.

“Whoops, try not to die.”

The enemies Yoichi anticipated were monsters and Demonfolk.

When dealing with ordinary people, if he misjudged his restraint, he had the strength to kill someone with a single blow, so Yoichi was fighting while carefully moderating his power.

Even that short uppercut from before only exerted power like a souped-up jab.

“Ugh, ugh… damn it… messing with me….”

Holding his shoulder, Souichi staggered to his feet.

Then, he glared at Karin standing directly in front of him.

“That’s it, I won’t forgive you… you guys! Kill them! Get serious!!”

Souichi ordered his members, but all he could hear in response were muffled groans.

“What are you doing? Hurry up and get these guys…”

Turning around, he saw a pile of men slumped on top of each other.

Only Yoichi and Alana were still standing.

“Wha… wha… what… damn it!”

Confused, Souichi regained his composure when he caught sight of the handgun in the corner of his vision and reached out with his left hand.

But then, Karin’s arrow struck, and the handgun was bounced up from the impact of the rubber bullet.

“Whoops.”

Yoichi caught the falling handgun.

“It’s over, Hongou.”

“Ugh…”

Karin calmly approached the slumping Souichi.

“I’m disappointed. You’ve really changed, haven’t you?”

Reflecting on Souichi’s actions and words since they reunited, she spoke the words above with genuine exasperation.

“S… shut up! What do you guys understand!! I obtained money beyond what ordinary people can get! Power! So, it’s only natural that I can’t stay the same as before, right!? Changing is natural!!”

“Aren’t you done yet? But Yoichi hasn’t changed at all.”

“Huh? What are you saying?”

“Yoichi has obtained greater power than you, Hongou, but he hasn’t changed at all.”

“Huh…really? This guy has that much power…?”

Looking back, Yoichi was standing in the midst of heaps of bodies, looking a bit embarrassed.

“As you can see, we can easily subdue 100 thugs. Of course, we have three people including me this time, but I believe he has shown enough power to win over you all on his own, don’t you think?”

“Well, just because he’s strong—.”

“But you’re talking about power earlier, you know?”

“Yes, maybe. But personal power is only a small part of it. What matters in the end is how many people you can influence!”

“Well, if you put it like that, then I guess yours is not much either since he made it easy enough to lure everyone of you with Huang Lao as bait.”

“What? Huang Lao as bait… All of this… wasn’t him?”

“Huh, did you really think you made it here on your own? Even with these a hundred thugs, you won’t be able to conquer one of Huang Lao’s bases, much more reach the center of one of their headquarters. You made it here because we have to lower the security to the point that we have to not let anyone connected to Huang Lao get involved with you. And you still ended up with your butt kicked by us alone.”

“Th, that’s…no way…”

“Do you see my point now? No matter what you do, Mr. Hongou, you’re no match for Yoichi.”

“Ugh…”

“As I said before, he’s amazing…”

“Karin, stop it already. Hongou’s HP is already zero.”

Feeling pity at Souichi’s slumped head, Yoichi reflexively stopped Karin.

“I think this is enough. Please leave the rest to us.”

When he was about to be escorted by Misato and Xihan, Huang Lao appeared.

At the same time, men in black suits also appeared from the stairwells and elevators, as well as emergency exits.

They skillfully took Souichi and his goons away.

“Well, now that the hindrances are out of the way, let’s have another toast. For real this time.”

With that, Huang Lao retuned to his room, followed by Misato and Xihan.

“I’m heading back as well.”

Alana also left, saying the same thing as she headed back to the venue.

Meanwhile, Karin stared blankly at the direction where Souichi was taken away.

“Hey, Karin.”

“What is it?”

“Am I really that amazing?”

“Really now?”

“It’s just that I happened to acquire a bunch of skills. I was just lucky.”

It’s true that Yoichi got lucky to get some skills.

But what about how he used these skills afterward?

Depending on the combination, anything can be obtained if he wills it.

Money can be earned endlessly.

And he can find out anything without any barriers.

If he has the will, he can even control the world.

But Yoichi doesn’t do such things.

_(If only I could use the [Appraisal+]._

_How many times would I regret learning things I didn’t need to know?_

_Could I control my curiosity and not look into other people’s thoughts?_

_And more importantly, could I who possesses the [Appraisal+] skill believe that my thoughts are not being pried into?_

_If anyone else had this skill, I would feel like my mind is being pried into all the time._

_But Yoichi doesn’t do such things._

_Why is that?_

_It’s strange._

_But somehow, I don’t feel like doubting it._

_That’s why I returned to Yoichi’s side._

_If someone like Souichi possessed the same power, I would be scared just thinking about it._

_With just money and influence, he became like a different person._

_But Yoichi, even after obtaining an overwhelming power, he didn’t change.)_

“Haven’t I mostly stayed the same since we first met?”

“Yes. And that’s amazing, don’t you think?”

“Amazing? What’s amazing about that?”

_I also like this absentmindedness of him as well._

“Well, in the end, it’s just luck.”

For Karin, it was not because Yoichi obtained the skills, but more that it was _the skills_ who obtained Yoichi.

As for the “luck” she was talking about, it was still undecided which side is.

“What was that for?”

“Never mind. We’ve kept everyone waiting for long, so we should go.”

Karin turned around and smiled at Yoichi before taking his arm.

Then she lead him back to where everyone else was waiting.

+++

## Chapter 9 – Huang Lao and Xihan 2 ※

After another toast and some small talk, the conversation turned to Huang Lao.

He himself revealed that he was a “left behind child” named Tanaka Shokichi.

“So, why ‘Huang Lao’?”

“In this country, that’s what they call an energetic old person… bah, more like an old geezer whose only good point is their vitality.”[[1]]

Now that she thought about it, Xihan then remembered that Huang Lao used to be called His Tian Da-in.2

At some point though, people started calling him Huang Lao, with the intended meaning as the above.

“You were born and raised around here, right?”

“Yeah, that’s right.”

“Was it tough? Because of the local atmosphere, or how do I put it…”

“Are you asking about the anti-Japanese sentiment?”

“Uh, yeah, kind of.”

Seeing Yoichi look a bit awkward, Huang Lao chuckled softly.

Then, after gulping down the remaining Shaoxing wine at the bottom of his glass, he spoke again.

“Yangyi, do you know when the anti-Japanese sentiment started in this country?”

“Um, since after the war… right?”

“It’s not from more than half a century ago. At most, maybe the last quarter-century or so.”

“Huh?!”

“Before that, Japan was just a country that was close by but not well understood. When you were a kid, Japan probably thought of this country the same way, don’t you think?”

Yoichi didn’t really remember, but Karin, sitting next to him, nodded in agreement, so it must have been true.

“You know that this country has messed up quite a bit since the war, right? It’s like they created an external enemy to distract from their own political failures. If the central government decides to do that, the whole country follows suit. For better or worse.”3

The recent development of this country was truly remarkable.

Walking around the town, Yoichi found many things that he thought were more convenient than in Japan.

Could this be a result of the country’s politics moving in a positive direction?

“Do you think it’s a good town?”

“Uh, well, yeah.”

“Thank you. But the countryside is terrible.”

What Yoichi had seen was just a very small part of this vast country.

It would be dangerous to judge the whole based on that alone.

There might be major problems hidden beneath the surface, but Yoichi decided there was no point in thinking about it further and downed the remaining half of his glass.

“Xihan told me. You want your sword back, don’t you?”

As if reading Yoichi’s attempt to change the subject, Huang Lao said this.

“Come with me.”

Huang Lao then led him to a place so large it could be called a small art museum.

Art objects were neatly displayed there.

“Everything in here, Xihan gave to me.”

“Heh heh, pretty amazing, huh?”

Xihan puffed out her chest proudly, but all of these were stolen goods.

Yoichi narrowed his eyes at her in a pointed way.

“Ah, ha ha… yeah, it’s not really something to brag about.”

Sensing Yoichi’s meaning, Xihan’s smile became strained as she scratched her cheek sheepishly.

Huang Lao, watching her, had a gentle smile on his face.

“Now then, Yangyi.”

Huang Lao’s expression changed, and he turned to face Yoichi directly.

“Could you return these to their rightful owners?”

“…That is…”

Yoichi hesitated on how to answer, and Huang Lao gave him a gentle smile.

“I won’t pry into your background. I won’t ask how you’ll do it either. Just tell me, can you do it or not?”

“Um, yeah… I can.”

“Good. Then let’s return all of this to Japan through you.”

At Huang Lao’s words, Xihan’s eyes widened.

“Grandpa, are you sure…?”

“Yes. I’ve enjoyed them enough. Thank you, Xihan.”

Saying this, Huang Lao patted Xihan’s head.

“Now then, how to entrust these to you…”

“About that, Huang Lao, would you believe me if I told you I can use magic?”

“Magic…?”

Here, “magic” refers not to techniques used in another world, but as a general term for supernatural abilities.

“How do you think I carried those art pieces out of the hotel in Akaho?”

“Hmm, I heard from Xihan. Judging by the video, it looked like a magic trick…”

At this point, Yoichi clearly demonstrated by holding his hand over a rather large gold folding screen nearby and storing it away.

“Wh-What?!”

Huang Lao exclaimed as the gold screen, so large it would be difficult to even lift, suddenly vanished.

“Well, you see, like this, I can transport anything here, no matter how much of it there is.”

Yoichi revealed his abilities to Huang Lao not so much because he trusted him, but because he figured it wouldn’t matter even if he knew.

He seemed to be mostly retired, and probably wouldn’t try to exploit Yoichi’s skills now.

Sure, he might help the government if asked, but basically, he seemed to be only thinking about enjoying his remaining years peacefully, so there was no benefit in hiding his skills from him.

Feeling a slight pang of guilt, but also partly for self-protection, Yoichi [Appraised] Huang Lao’s thoughts and came to that conclusion.

He chuckled softly. “Well, well… to still be surprised at my age. Living a long life really is something, isn’t it?”

After saying this, sounding genuinely impressed, Huang Lao turned his back to Yoichi.

“You wanted that sword, didn’t you? This way.”

Huang Lao started walking, leading Yoichi and the others to a space where swords were displayed.

Then, from among the lined-up swords, he casually lifted a large tachi, a long sword.

“Was it this one, perhaps?”

Huang Lao, who looked like nothing more than a frail old man, was perhaps surprisingly strong physically. Slightly surprised by this, Yoichi accepted the tachi.

“Yes, this is definitely it.”

Yoichi Appraised the tachi he received and confirmed it was the one he was looking for.

“Could I take everything here?”

“Ah, I won’t go back on my word. Suit yourself.”

Many items in Huang Lao’s collection were from the Kamakura to Muromachi periods [roughly 12th – 16th centuries].

Especially when it came to swords, he seemed to prefer those with high combat capability over those that were merely art pieces. Besides the tachi he was after, the collection included excellent katana (long swords), kodachi (short swords), and wakizashi (side swords).

While katana, which are considered the longer sword in a two-sword set, were practical weapons, wakizashi, the shorter sword, and kodachi, which fall in between, weren’t as often used in actual combat.

However, [Appraisal+] assured him of their performance, as they were forged by master swordsmiths of the era.

“Then, please store the rest of them as well.”

“Understood.”

Because the collection included items from this country and others besides Japan, Yoichi selected only the Japanese items to store away.

“It’s gotten quite empty, hasn’t it?”

Huang Lao looked around the now-bare collection room, a wistful expression on his face, looking somehow lonely.

Xihan, watching Huang Lao, also looked a little sad.

“Huang Lao, if you don’t mind, would you like to display these instead?”

Perhaps feeling sorry for the two of them, Yoichi took out some of the art pieces he’d brought from the Scarlet Spica Hotel the other day and arranged them.

“Is this… alright?”

“Well, there are various reasons these things ended up in the black market besides stealing them, you see.”

Some are put up for sale voluntarily by their owners, while others, though discarded without their value being known, are found by chance. Not everything is stolen goods.

Of course, these are valuable cultural assets of Japan, so if there are no owners, the country, local government, or some organization should possess them.

“Just until you get tired of them though, then I’ll take them back.”

Yoichi thought that maybe it would be alright to leave them with Huang Lao for a while, just to brighten his remaining years.

He wasn’t some hero of justice or anything.

“Thank you. I will treasure them.”

“Yangyi, thank you very much. Let me thank you on behalf of us both.”

Huang Lao and Xihan bowed their heads together.

“Heh heh…”

“Heh heh… Ahahaha…!”

Raising their heads at the same time, the two looked at each other and then began to chuckle.

“Xihan, take care.”

“Yeah. Grandpa, you too, live a long life!”

Xihan said with a smile, though faint tears were welling up in her eyes.

〇●〇●

Having finished all their errands, Yoichi and the others left Huang Lao’s place.

“So, Xihan’s coming with us, huh?”

“Yup.”

“Are you really okay with leaving Huang Lao?”

“Grandpa basically gave me the boot a while back, but I didn’t have anything else to do.”

There was also the option of being directly employed by the government, but Huang Lao wouldn’t allow it.

Perhaps he was planning to set her free someday.

“So, did you find something you wanted to do?”

“Not really, but hanging with Yoichi sounds like it’ll be fun.”

### Afterword

About the Author

Author: Ho-chi

Thanks to you all, this work has reached the milestone of 10 volumes!

Thank you very much, author Ho-chi here.

This volume focuses on Karin, who didn’t get much spotlight in the previous volume, and the new character Xihan. Unfortunately, because Karin wore a cheongsam in volume 5, Alana in a new costume stole the cover from her again! (lol)

But I made sure the illustrations in the book really focused on her, so please forgive me! Well then, from the next volume onward, the story is going to take a big turn.

I’ll be intricately weaving together and resolving the foreshadowing I’ve scattered here and there, so please continue to enjoy the series!

### Translator Notes:

1. I don’t know why the author put it that way, and I’m not too familiar with the Chinese culture, but a simple google search about Huang Lao (spelled 黄(Yellow) 老(Old Person) isn’t just an “energetic old person” at all. Or rather, back in the Han Dynasty, Huang Lao was the most influential Chinese school of thought. Hell, even the characters were a portmanteau, with “Huang” being the Yellow Emperor, and “Lao” being Laozi, literally meaning “Old Master”.[↰](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/stabbingwithasyringe-translated-works/what-failure-to-transition-success/what-failure-to-transition-volume-9-chapter-9epilogueafterword/#subscript1)

2. Tian Da-in (田大人) came from how the characters of Tanaka Shokichi (田(Tián) 中(zhōng) 昭(Zhāo) 吉(jí)) is pronounced in Chinese. Yes, it is referring to the first character in his name (田(Tian)). Da-in means His/Her Excellency/Lordship which denotes the authority of the person, most often political. So Tian Da-in (田大人) loosely translates to His Excellency/Lordship Tian but I chose to keep the former coz it doesn’t sound right in this translation. Also, I want to keep the western terms on the isekai world (which is western medieval fantasy-themed) and eastern terms to the east as much as possible.[↰](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/stabbingwithasyringe-translated-works/what-failure-to-transition-success/what-failure-to-transition-volume-9-chapter-9epilogueafterword/#subscript2)

3. The part where the “Japan hate propaganda” starting in Mainland China late is more or less the truth in a way. Or rather, back then, the current government (People’s Republic of China, governed by the Chinese Communist Party or CCP) is even viewing Japan in a positive light as they eliminated their opposing party that was leading the mainland at that time, now currently in the island of Taiwan (Republic of China, governed by the Kuomintang or Nationalist Party of China or KMT). It was even documented the interview with Mao Zedong when the Japanese government conducted a formal apology that time for the atrocities they made during the war that he even straight up expressed his gratitude to Japan’s brutal invasion. As if not for them crushing the Kuomintang, they wouldn’t have been able to take China easily from the KMT.[↰](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/stabbingwithasyringe-translated-works/what-failure-to-transition-success/what-failure-to-transition-volume-9-chapter-9epilogueafterword/#subscript3)

# What, Failure to Transition!? - Volume 10 - Prologue

In a chamber in the royal castle of the Kingdom of Sansrival.

Lamps were set firmly in place in the windowless room, bathing the interior in ample light. Even so, a subtle air of darkness permeated the space.

“Preposterous! Controlling a horde of monsters? Utterly impossible. He’d have to be some kind of Demon Lord!”

The gruff voice of a man echoed in the room.

The speaker was William, the Margrave of Salis, and Alana’s father.

He was currently undergoing questioning within the royal castle.

Present were the King, the Prime Minister, high-ranking officials, and noble aristocrats, encircling William as he stood on a platform in the center of the room, resembling a witness stand.

The King and nobles were positioned on a dais, looking down upon the Margrave as the interrogation proceeded.

“And isn’t it true that this so-called ‘Demon’ of yours did, in fact, appear?”

A youthful voice cut through the dimly lit room.

The voice belonged to a handsome young man with dull blond hair.

“Yes, that is correct. And it was by defeating that Demon that the current monster stampede was brought to an end.”

“Truly defeated?”

“…What exactly are you implying, Count Colborne?”

The young man’s name was Patrick Colborne.

He was the current head of the Count Colborne family, the main house of the Salis lineage.

Though just turned thirty, he had been his father’s right-hand man since his twenties, and in recent years had effectively seized control of the earldom’s affairs.

His father had recently retired citing illness, allowing Patrick to ascend to the headship.

“Isn’t it possible you allied with this Demon, merely driving back the monster horde temporarily? Rumors suggest they are amassing strength to attack the capital in due time.”

“Such slander is beyond the pale.”

“You watch your tongue, you country nobleman.”

Patrick’s cold retort caused William to knit his brows.

Though the Colbornes were the main house, a Margrave typically held a higher rank than a Count.

However, the kingdom’s nobility system held its own peculiarities.

In the Empire, for instance, a Margrave might nominally equate to a Marquis, in practice wielding influence second only to a Duke.

The Kingdom, while borrowing somewhat from the imperial noble system, also incorporated its own unique elements.

And the Salis family, branching off from the Colbornes, had repeatedly been elevated in rank for their contributions to frontier development and defense against monster stampedes.

Just as the Salis family was on the cusp of being raised to Count rank, fierce opposition erupted from the main Colborne house.

The crown couldn’t easily disregard the opinions of influential upper nobles within the kingdom, yet neither could they fail to reward the Salis family for their merits.

Thus, the royal family, to appease both houses, treated the Margrave as a “noble who governs the frontier”—an ambiguous designation.

In essence, it was a special status, recognized even by Dukes within the kingdom. But it is also for this reason that the Colborne family was able to consistently look down upon the Salis.

The Salis family, for their part, generally avoided contact with the Colbornes, and when circumstances required their presence together, they often adopted a stance of deference, as the branch family honoring the main house.

Originally, the Salis were a family of warriors, ill-suited for courtly intrigue.

“My apologies. Then, upon what basis do you assert that I have joined hands with those Demons?”

Though his words expressed apology, William offered no hint of it in his expression or tone. Patrick’s eyebrows twitched, but he quickly composed himself, snapping the report in his hand with a flick of his finger.

“Compared to the scale of this monster stampede, weren’t the casualties remarkably low?”

“That is solely due to the valiant efforts of my town’s military and the adventurers within it.”

“There are also reports of a Greater Land Turtle appearing?”

“That is…”

The name “Greater Land Turtle” sparked murmurs in the room.

The kingdom had a history of towns being ravaged by Land Turtles, enormous turtle-like monsters.

If a Greater Land Turtle, a monster even superior to those, had appeared, it would constitute a national crisis.

“Rumor has it, it was even Emperor class, wouldn’t you say?”

The murmurs intensified.

A Greater Land Turtle Emperor… that would be a crisis not just for the kingdom, but potentially for the entire empire.

“Silence!”

The Prime Minister’s sharp command brought a hush to the room.

“That is… merely a rumor, is it not?”

William, looking uneasy, offered a weak rebuttal.

The Greater Land Turtle Emperor had been defeated by TOROKOTEN, led by Yoichi, and its corpse had been taken into his [Infinite Storage+].

William and Celestin had decided to keep it secret, fearing a public announcement would cause widespread panic.

“However, there are eyewitness accounts from adventurers. Surely, exceptional adventurers from the frontier who quelled a monster stampede with minimal casualties wouldn’t be mistaken?”

Eyewitnesses to the Greater Land Turtle Emperor were not numerous.

While a gag order had been issued, words, like wildfire, spread regardless, and information had leaked.

“Furthermore, in the Jana Forest, traces have been found of something massive carving a path through the trees, wouldn’t you agree?”

“That is…”

Patrick wears a triumphant smile.

“Is it even possible to erase such a massive monster without a trace? Wouldn’t it be more natural to think you joined hands with those Demons and made it retreat into the depths of the forest?”

“However, those are just rumors, aren’t they? Isn’t it a bit of a stretch to brand someone a rebel based on vague information?”

“I heard that Demons appeared in the northern frontier the other day.”

William frowned at the sudden change of subject.

Ignoring that, Patrick continued.

“And I heard that an adventurer party called TOROKOTEN was quite active in subduing them.”

“…Yes, they are adventurers that our town is proud of.”

“I also hear your daughter Alana belongs to it?”

William sensed something vulgar in Patrick’s expression as he said that.

“And?”

“I hear she’s also quite the popular figure in the northern frontier.”

“That is due to Alana’s achievements.”

“Furthermore, I hear adventurers from the Empire have been visiting Meilgrad repeatedly.”

“Adventurers have no borders. It’s their freedom to operate wherever they please.”

“Even going all the way from the northern edge of the human sphere to the southern edge?”

“Such things happen, I suppose.”

An unpleasant atmosphere hung in the air.

“Alexander Ballschmiede and Emma Klemperer. I hear they are so excellent in the Empire they are called heroes.”

“Yes, that seems to be the case.”

“You’re not planning to collude with these excellent adventurers and join hands with the Empire, are you?”

A murmur rose again.

More than one or two people must have considered what would happen if they were attacked from both north and south simultaneously.

“What are you saying?!”

William’s roar, like thunder, instantly silenced the room.

“It’s common knowledge even for children that guilds are neutral and adventurers don’t side with either nation!”

“That’s right, guilds are neutral.”

Influenced perhaps by William’s roar, Patrick continued talking without taking issue with his tone.

“But what about the Meilgrad Branch?”

“What’s that?”

“Isn’t it true that the Adventurer’s Guild is governed by your father-in-law, and the Mage’s Guild by your wife?”

“Are you saying my father-in-law and wife are privatizing the guilds!?”

“That’s not all. Your daughter Alana is said to be Meilgrad’s top adventurer, and her party members are ranking up at an abnormal speed, aren’t they?”

“That’s considering their achievements—”

“I also hear you expelled a promising young adventurer called ‘Red Flash.’ Despite his achievements in the northern frontier, they say he retreated to a rural town instead of returning to Meilgrad.”

“That’s because they wished for success in their hometown—”

“I wonder about that. Could it be they shunned Meilgrad, which is dominated by the Salis family?”

William’s eyebrows shot up and his eyes became bloodshot at Patrick’s words, which could only be interpreted as an insult.

“You’ve been saying whatever you please since earlier! Wasn’t it you who tried to attack my daughter with despicable methods?!”

“That’s just utter nonsense. What proof do you have?”

“Proof—”

“Let me tell you, I am merely listing facts.”

“What?”

“The casualties are too low for the scale of the monster stampede, there are eyewitnesses to the Greater Land Turtle Emperor yet no corpse, adventurers affiliated with both north and south are going back and forth, the Meilgrad Guilds are governed by those connected to the Salis family, and a talented young adventurer left the frontier.”

“Guh… Even so, how does that become evidence of rebellion!?”

“Certainly, mentioning rebellion might have been a bit of an overstatement.”

Patrick paused there, turning to face the King.

“Based on the facts I just presented, please consider what should be done about William Salis.”

Saying so, Patrick bowed deeply.

The King watched the proceedings with a blank expression, while the Prime Minister beside him wore an exasperated look.

And many in the room were perplexed.

The Empire’s invasion coming from the north.

The monster stampede coming from the south.

The Sansrival Kingdom was constantly battling these two threats.

For the past decade or so, there had been ominous movements in the Demon Lord’s territory in the northern Empire. Added to pressure from various guilds, the two nations had established a non-aggression pact.

While minor skirmishes near the border couldn’t be completely eliminated, the anxiety from the north had largely been dispelled.

Thanks to Meilgrad, which was developed beyond the Wilderness of Death, it became clear that the Jana Forest was the starting point for the monster stampede from the south.

Soldiers and adventurers residing in the frontier were now able to provide a certain level of defense, and the anxiety from that direction had also mostly disappeared.

However, these underlying fears are hard to shake off, and many people feel uneasy, wondering if another calamity might befall them.

Especially when rumors circulated that “Border Count” William had subdued the southern monster groups running wild and might one day invade the kingdom, all hell broke loose.

Various opinions flew about, the room became chaotic, and eventually, things calmed down.

“Border Count William of Salis will be placed under house arrest in the royal capital.”

There is no clear evidence of rebellion.

Nor can it be definitively said that there is suspicion.

However, leaving him at large is frightening.

Therefore, the king, the prime minister, officials, and nobles decided to confine William to the royal capital for a while under surveillance.

“Patrick!”

As the interrogation was dismissed and the young man was about to leave the room, William called out to him.

“What was all that about?”

“What was ‘what’ about?”

“What happened to the kind-hearted young man Patrick, who cherished Henry like a younger brother and revered me as an uncle!?”

“Nothing.”

Patrick replied expressionlessly to William’s almost shouting question.

“From the moment I was born into the Colborne family, I swore allegiance to the kingdom and have lived only for the kingdom’s benefit. And I will continue to live that way.”

“I… am becoming a harm to the kingdom? You really think I’m going to rebel!?”

“Hmph…”

Leaving a cold smile behind, Patrick left.

Rumors began to circulate that Border Count William of Salis was suspected of treason and detained at a facility in the royal capital.

In reality, William was merely ordered to remain confined to his residence in the royal capital, but such rumors started to spread.

### Chapter 2 – The Situation in the Royal Capital 2 ※

“And that seems to be the whole story.”

In the reception room of the Adventurer’s Guild, Yoichi explained what he had confirmed using his [Appraisal+] skill.

Present at this gathering were Alana, Karin, Misato, Samantha, and Xihan—the TOKOROTEN members—as well as Vista, the butler of the Salis family; Celestin, the Adventurer’s Guild Master and William’s father-in-law; and Hortense, the Mages’ Guild’s master and also William’s wife—a total of nine people.

Alec and Emma, who had been with them in the training grounds until just moments before, were sent back to the town of Coruso using [Return+], as it was judged best that they not be present considering the circumstances.

In addition, it was decided among themselves that the party that aas famous in the Empire “did not visit this city” like some sort of pseudo-gag order.

“It seems the report from the mansion was just a rumor after all.”

Opening the conversation, Vista held a complex expression on his face, yet he also sighed with relief at the end, as if somewhat reassured.

Once you reach a certain rank of nobility, you will have your own communication network between the royal capital and your territory.

Regarding the house arrest this time, Henry had not told anyone other than Hazel, his personal attendant.

Because Hazel, who swore absolute loyalty to Henry, did not leak the information to anyone else, the residents of the mansion could not accurately know the reason for William’s confinement and were swayed by Patrick’s rumors, which were then sent by the informants to them.

“According to the Guild, it was said that there were deficiencies in the report of the monster stampede, so he only received a standby order. We thought it was just for another round of questioning… but it seems it’s going to get more troublesome from here,” Celestin said, then glanced at Hortense.

But the expression that came back to him was a stern and silent one.

Celestin had seen his daughter with such an expression only a few times in his long life.

“Well, in any case, it was good that we coordinated our information early.”

Alana spoke as if to digress the topic.

She, who had been stunned for a while after receiving the initial report from the Yoichi’s [Appraisal+], visited the Adventurer’s Guild accompanied by Vista upon Yoichi’s suggestion. This is to convey the information and to match them to Celestin and the others had received.

They had Hortense, Alana’s mother and William’s wife, and also the Mages’ Guild Master, summoned, and after comparing their respective information, Yoichi summarized the findings of his [Appraisal+] investigation.

“…But what are those guys in the royal capital thinking? There have been several attempts to weaken the Salis family’s power before, but if they do that now and the fighting strength of the frontier declines, it will ultimately be nothing but a loss for the kingdom.”

“Isn’t it a case of ‘the grass is always greener on the other side of the fence’?”

When Yoichi replied this to Celestin, about half of the people present, who were from another world, tilted their heads in confusion.

“…What does that mean?”

“It means that other people’s lives or situations always seem better than your own. The nobles in the royal capital must be envious of the wealth and power the frontier is having.”

“Ruling this place is tough, you know?”

“Then let me put it in this way. If I remember correctly, it also means that people only see the _good parts_ of other people’s things. Or rather, they only see what they _want to see_, conveniently ignoring the bad parts, those kinds of people.”

“Hmm… that’s a feeling I don’t really understand.”

Next to Celestin, who was folding his arms and tilting his head, Alana was also folding her arms just like her grandfather.

“Even so, to think that Patrick was the one who sent those thugs… If only we have known this earlier…”

She muttered to herself in a puzzled tone, looking down with a troubled expression.

Hearing that, Yoichi looked at the princess knight with a slightly exasperated tone.

“Sorry, Alana, but that was already investigated and reported way back.”

“Huh, was it?”

Yes. The attack by the three thugs that triggered Yoichi and Alana’s meeting had been thoroughly investigated by [Appraisal+], including the background relationships, and reported to William and Celestin.

He hadn’t been able to explain it to Alana on the spot, but in the meantime, that incident had become insignificant to her, so he had missed the opportunity to talk about it.

Celestin asked, his voice slightly tinged with anger as he remembered the incident, looking around in bewilderment.

Yue Fei, a hero of the Southern Song dynasty, repeatedly repelled invasions from the Jin dynasty, which controlled the north, and diligently protected his country.

He was a man of fervent loyalty, even tattooing the words ‘Serve the Country with Utmost Loyalty’ on his back. However, when peace was established with the enemy Jin dynasty, he was accused of treason by Chancellor Qin Hui, who feared his influence, and was tortured and executed.

Questioning his death, Yue Fei’s colleague demanded of Qin Hui, “Where is the evidence of treason?!” Qin Hui’s reply was “莫須有” (Moshūyū), meaning “it cannot be said for certain that it is impossible” – in essence, “Maybe it exists, maybe not.”

Humanity has repeatedly learned the hard way about the consequences of neglecting logistics—securing and supplying military necessities and provisions.

It was no longer a town that could be sustained by hunting and gathering alone.

“Well, you see, just being on the receiving end doesn’t really suit my nature…”

“Eh? Eh?”

“Fufufu… Don’t worry, I don’t intend to resort to violence. I just thought I’d take the lead this time.”

The Princess Knight continued to look down at Yoichi, and moved one hand behind her back.

Alana’s other hand, a little stiff, touched his now-small penis.

“Hey, um, I just came a lot, you know? Maybe we should take a break first…”

“Xihan taught me about this,”

“Eh?”

Alana’s hand, which had been touching his penis, moved past his testicles and touched the perineum area.

“He said if you press here, Mister Yoichi will get energized.”

“UwoooOh…!”

Yoichi let out a groan as her fingertip pressed firmly on the area between his genitals and anus, slightly closer to the testicles.

It was a pressure point that Xihan had discovered through her ‘arts of the bedchamber,’ a point that stimulated Yoichi’s erection, and thanks to the stimulation, blood began to flow back into his limp penis.

However, it wasn’t yet enough to be called an erection.

“L-look… it’s no use like that. Let’s take a break and, you know, do it normally…”

“If I remember correctly, it’s about directing the flow of ‘chi’ or something, right? Hmm, should I infuse it with mana instead?”

“W-wait, st— unghh!!”

_――Splurururururut! Splurururt! Splururt!_

Suddenly, a large amount of mana was poured into the pressure point, causing Yoichi to ejaculate instantly, bypassing the erection phase.

“Huh!? Did I get it wrong…?”

However, Alana, as if she had anticipated this, showed no particular surprise. She put a hand to her chin and tilted her head with a deliberately clueless expression.

“That… you did that on purpose, didn’t you…?”

“Now, now, I wonder…”

“Hey, this kind of thing isn’t good, you know? A little knowledge is a dangerous thing…”

“Fufu…”

Alana smiled at Yoichi, whose face was contorted.

However, it was a truly contrived, mischievous smile.

“Eek…”

“Don’t worry, I’m a genius.”

“That’s… definitely not right— ohohh…!”

Mana was poured in again, but this time in a smaller amount than before, preventing ejaculation.

Still, it was swelling to the point of bursting.

“Now then, Mister Yoichi. The night is still young, you know?”

“Nooooo…!”

〇●〇●

Meanwhile, outside the motorhome, Karin, Misato, and Xihan were chatting while leaning against a griffin.

The griffin had been flying for a whole day and, although it was being regularly rejuvenated by Misato’s magic, seemed to still be tired.

It stood there unsteadily until the harness was removed, and once Misato gave it a final magical healing, it lay down and started to snore.

“Wow, it’s so fluffy!”

The griffin’s feathers were smooth as silk, while its body fur was soft like a cat’s.

The three of them originally rested in a tent, but since the starry sky was beautiful, they brought chairs outside to sit and enjoy.

Xihan ended up leaning against the griffin, only to find it quite comfortable. Even though it was trained, a griffin is still a magical creature, so leaning on its body was a dangerous act; however, the griffin showed no signs of waking, perhaps due to its fatigue. Even if it did wake up, the three were not ones to be easily dealt with by a griffin.

“The stars are beautiful,” said Karin, dazzled as she looked up at the sky.

While she was moved by the abundance of stars stretching above them, she felt an odd sense of unfamiliarity.

“Thank you, Misato.”

“Oh, i-it’s nothing, really.”

The desert night was cold, but thanks to Misato’s magic, the temperature and humidity around them remained comfortable.

“We’re really in another world,” noted Xihan suddenly.

“What’s with you, Xihan, saying something like that out of the blue?” Karin asked.

“The arrangement of the stars is totally different, right? That’s how I realized it,” Xihan replied.

“Oh, so that’s why…” Karin responded. It seemed that the source of her odd feeling was the different star arrangements.

Even Karin, who wasn’t knowledgeable about constellations, could sense the difference from their original world.

Misato nodded as if she had also realized this after Xihan’s comment.

“By the way, do you like the starry sky? That’s… unexpected,” Karin mused.

“True, true. Xihan, are you a romantic at heart?” Misato also teased.

Xihan let out a deep sigh as if exasperated by their comments.

“What are you guys talking about? Astrology is like our family tradition.”

“Astrology? You mean like fortune-telling?” Karin inquired.

“I can tell Karin’s imagination is a bit naive, connecting astrology directly with fortune-telling in one go.”

“Oh, is that so bad?”

Meanwhile, Misato also blushed slightly and looked down, suggesting that she too thought of fortune-telling when hearing about astrology.

“So, can you tell fortunes? Or not?” Karin asked.

“Well, divination is about gathering information, so it’s a skill useful for spies, and it can be an icebreaker in conversations.”

“Oh, so you can do it.”

“Not just astronomy, but palmistry, physiognomy, four pillars of destiny, Nine Star Chi—basically everything. If you have stalks, I can do I Ching divination, and if there’s a turtle shell, I can even do turtle divination.”1

“What are stalks?”

“Those thin bamboo sticks used by Asian-style fortune tellers.”

“Oh, those ones!”

“Ah, Y-Yoichi has a turtle shell, right?” This time it was Misato who remembered something.

“You mean that Greater Land Emperor something? That’s way too big,” Xihan stated, laughing as she shook her head.

“Oh, the rumored giant turtle? It’d take years to crack and open that thing!” Karin added, joining in the laughter.

“Right, what should we divine? Love fortunes, maybe?” After the bliss died out, Karin asked again.

“B-but as for love fortunes… we don’t really need one right now, do we?” Misato responded.

“True. Our love seems to be going just fine,” Karin said with a smile.

“Indeed. Though I think Yoichi has some woman trouble in his future,” Xihan speculated.

“Really? But isn’t he having a good time?”

“P-plus, he certainly seems to be enjoying himself lately, doesn’t he?”

“Hmm, I’m not so sure about that…”

At Xihan’s words, all their eyes turned toward the motorhome.

The magical protections prevented sound from leaking out, but controlling vibrations was difficult, especially those transmitted from inside to outside.

“Seems quite intense in there.”

Karin commented, as the motorhome swayed and creaked in the open wilderness.

“I-I hope Yoichi is handling it well.”

Misato said with concern.

“Even with that intensity, I’m sure it’s going fine.”

Xihan reassured.

“Or maybe he’s getting more than he bargained for?”

“T-that would be fine too. Lately, he’s been getting a bit full of himself.”

Recently, there had been an increase in women around Yoichi. He reunited with Karin, met Misato, and saved Alana.

After various events, Yoichi continued traveling with the three, eventually meeting Charlotte in the casino city.

Since then, he’s received plenty of support and, depending on the timing, has gotten close with some of them.

And now the alchemical blacksmith Samantha has joined. And although they didn’t become full comrades, during the Toudou family dispute and the Demon Invasion, he was getting along with the ‘Red Flash’ girls Mina, Jessica, and Greta.

And just recently, Xihan became part of the group too.

“Maybe another woman will join?” Karin speculated.

“Not sure,” Misato replied.

“I feel like Amanda might,” Xihan guessed.

“No way, that’s impossible,” Misato stated.

“Yeah, I highly doubt it’d be a Demon,” Karin agreed.

“Oh, I’ve never met one, so I don’t know, but they’re supposed to be like enemies of humanity, right?” Xihan asked for confirmation.

“Exactly. No matter how fickle Yoichi is, he wouldn’t get involved with a Demon.”

“Haha, right, that’s a bit too far-fetched.”

“Y-yeah, I don’t think it could happen…right?”

As Yoichi engaged with Alana, and was getting pushed back in return, a peaceful girls’ talk was taking place outside the motorhome.

### Translator Notes:

1. The original raws used the word Astronomy (天文) rather than Astrology (占星学) here. But since using the former is kinda inappropriate, I chose the latter. Also, all of the things mentioned by Xihan here are all sorts of divination practices used waaay back in ancient times, especially in Ancient China.

Astrology is the general term for the divinatory practice that interprets the positions and movements of celestial objects to gain insights into human affairs and events. The horoscopes, the zodiac, tarot readings, Chinese astrology, Mayan astrology (which was famous back then for its 2012 end-of-the-world hoax) and other forms.

Palmistry is the practice of interpreting personality and predicting future events by analyzing the physical features of the hands, particularly the lines, shapes, and mounts on the palm.

Physiognomy does the same but with the face.

Four Pillars of Destiny, aka “Ba-Zi” is a Chinese astrological concept that a person’s destiny or fate can be divined by the two sexagenary cycle characters assigned to their birth year, month, day, and hour.

Nine Star Ki is a form of astrology based on your birth year, month, and day. There is one with a forecast for 2025 found here

I Ching/Yijing Divination is one of the oldest forms of divination in ancient China, so old that it was the basis for divination practice for centuries across the Far East.

![](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/04/oracle-turtle-shell-for-divination.jpg?w=250)

Oracle Turtle Shell with inscriptions used in I Ching Divination

![](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/04/bamboo-stalks-for-i-ching-divination.jpg?w=250)

Bamboo Stalks used in I Ching Divination (from Wikipedia)

It comes in all forms like reading the lines on the turtle shell, or using yarrow stalks (from bamboo) assigned with numbers, though the method as to “why” they assigned such numbers was already lost in times.[↰](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/stabbingwithasyringe-translated-works/what-failure-to-transition-success/what-failure-to-transition-volume-10-chapter-4/#subscript1)
